Minimum Pregnancy Period and Paternity of a Purchased Slave Wife
Explains six-month minimum pregnancy period and its legal effect on paternity after divorce and purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the six-month minimum pregnancy rule to determine paternity in scenarios where a man divorces and then purchases his slave wife, including the distinction for two divorces.

Core Idea
A child born less than six months after purchase is from the marriage; after six months, from ownership.

The Hanafi school establishes a minimum pregnancy period of six months derived from the Quran. This lesson unpacks how this rule interacts with changes in marital status and ownership, specifically when a man divorces his slave wife and later purchases her. The ruling hinges on the time between purchase and birth, and the number of divorces can extend the attribution period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is attributing paternity when a divorced slave wife gives birth after being purchased. The ruling is that if birth occurs less than six months from purchase, the child is from the marriage (incumbent without claim). If six months or more, the child is from the slave woman (ownership).
The ruling is wajib (obligatory) when conditions are met.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 46:15: 'And His gestation and weaning are thirty months.' This establishes the minimum pregnancy period by deducting the typical weaning period of two years.
Thubut is qati, dalala is zanni (requires deduction).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse combines gestation and weaning as thirty months. Assuming weaning is typically twenty-four months, the minimum gestation is six months. This is the legal basis for the minimum period.
The deduction is accepted by the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the rule to the base case (one divorce)
With one divorce (whether irrevocable, khul', or revocable), the rule is straightforward: if birth occurs within six months of purchase, paternity is from the marriage; if after, from ownership.
If the divorce was before consummation, different conditions apply as mentioned in the footnote.
5
Distinguish the case of two divorces
If the divorce was two (the maximum for a slave wife), she becomes severely prohibited. Intercourse after purchase is not permitted, so conception is presumed to have occurred before the divorce. Therefore, paternity is attributed up to two years from the time of divorce.
This is based on the principle of 'carrying affairs of Muslims upon righteousness' (hamlan li umur al-muslimin 'ala al-salah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأقلها ستة أشهر. ومن نكح أمة فطلقها فشراها، فإن ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر منذ شراها لزمه وإلا فلا؛ لأنه إذا كان بين الشراء والولادة أقل من ستة أشهر كان العلوق سابقاً على الشراء، فهو ولد منكوحته، فيلزم بلا دعوى. أما إذا كانت المدة ستة أشهر أو أكثر، فالولد ولد مملوكته؛ لأن العلوق أمر [1] قوله: ستة أشهر؛ لقوله في سورة الأحقاف: وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلَثُونَ شَهْرًا، كما مر تقديره. [2] قوله: فهو ولد منكوحته؛ لأن قبل الشراء كانت معتدة له، أو زوجة له، ونسب ولد كل واحد منها يثبت بلا دعوة. [3] قوله: ولد مملوكته؛ هذا إذا كان الطلاق واحداً بائناً أو خلعاً أو رجعياً، فإن كان طلقها ثنتين يثبت النسب إلى سنتين من وقت الطلاق؛ لأنها حرمت عليه حرمة غليظة؛ إذ طلاق الأمة ثنتان، وقرؤها حيضتان على ما مر في موضعه، فلا يحل وطئها بالشراء، ما لم تنكح زوجاً غيره. فلا يقضي بكون العلوق في أقرب الأوقات بل من أبعدها، حملاً لأمور المسلمين على الصلاح، وأبعد الأزمان هو ما قبل الطلاق، فيلزمه الولد إذا جاءت به لأقل من سنتين من وقت الطلاق، وأما إذا كان الطلاق واحداً يحل له وطؤها بعد الشراء بملك (1) أي بعد الدخول طلقة؛ لأنه لو كان قبل الدخول فإن جاءت به لأكثر من ستة أشهر من وقت الطلاق لا يلزمه، وإن كان لأقل منه لزمه إذا ولدته لتمام ستة أشهر أو أكثر من وقت العقد، وإن كان لأقل لا يلزمه. وأيضاً تكون واحدة بائنة أو رجعية؛ لأنه إذا كان ثنتين يثبت النسب إلى سنتين من وقت الطلاق للحرمة الغليظة فلا يضاف العلوق إلا إلى ما قبله؛ لأنها لا تحل بالشراء.
And its minimum is six months. And whoever marries a slave woman, divorces her, then purchases her: if she gives birth at less than six months from her purchase, it is incumbent upon him, otherwise not; because if between the purchase and birth is less than six months, the conception was before the purchase, so it is the child of his married wife, so it is incumbent without claim. But if the period is six months or more, the child is the child of his female slave; because conception is... [1] His saying: six months; due to His saying in Surah Al-Ahqaf: 'And his gestation and weaning are thirty months,' as its estimation has passed. [2] His saying: so it is the child of his married wife; because before the purchase she was either in 'iddah from him or his wife, and the lineage of the child of each of them is established without claim. [3] His saying: child of his female slave; this is if the divorce was one irrevocable or khul' or revocable; but if he divorced her twice, lineage is established up to two years from the time of divorce; because she has become forbidden to him with a severe prohibition; since divorce of a slave woman is two, and her 'iddah is two menstruations as has passed in its place, so intercourse is not permitted by purchase unless she marries another husband. So it is not judged that conception is at the nearest time but from the furthest, carrying the affairs of Muslims upon righteousness, and the furthest time is before the divorce, so the child is incumbent if she brings it at less than two years from the time of divorce. And as for when the divorce is one, he may have intercourse by ownership... (1) i.e., after consummation once; because if before consummation, and she brings it more than six months from divorce, it is not incumbent; if less, it is incumbent if she gives birth at a full six months or more from the time of contract; if less, it is not incumbent. Also it is one irrevocable or revocable; because if two, lineage is established up to two years from divorce due to severe prohibition, so conception is not attributed except to before it, because she is not permissible by purchase.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah clarifies the minimum period of pregnancy (six months) and its application to a specific scenario: a man who marries a slave woman, divorces her, and then purchases her. The ruling is that if she gives birth less than six months after the purchase, the child is attributed to the marriage and its lineage is established without the need for a claim. If six months or more have passed, the child is considered the child of the slave woman (i.e., belonging to the master by ownership). The proof is the Quranic verse (46:15) that gestation and weaning total thirty months, implying a minimum pregnancy of six months. The commentator further distinguishes based on the type and number of divorces. If the divorce was one (whether irrevocable, khul', or revocable), the same rule applies. However, if he divorced her with two divorces (the maximum for a slave woman), she becomes severely prohibited, so intercourse after purchase is not permitted. Consequently, the conception is presumed to have occurred at the furthest possible time, which is before the divorce, so lineage is established up to two years from the time of divorce. The footnote adds that if the divorce was before consummation, different conditions apply. This passage illustrates how the Hanafi school uses the minimum pregnancy period to resolve paternity disputes when ownership or marital status changes.

Key Terms
العلوق (al-'uluq): Conception; the moment the child is conceived in the womb.
منكوحته (mankūḥatuhu): His married wife (the woman he has nikah with).
مملوكته (mamlūkatuhu): His female slave (whom he owns).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man divorces his slave wife (one revocable divorce), then purchases her, and she gives birth six months after the purchase, what is the ruling on the child's paternity?
A) The child is from the marriage and lineage is established without claim.
B) The child is from the marriage but lineage requires a claim.
C) The child is considered the offspring of the slave woman (mamlukah).
D) The child is not attributed to anyone.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the six-month minimum pregnancy period, derived from the Quran, to resolve paternity when a divorced slave wife is purchased, with a special two-year extension for cases of two divorces.

The Four Ranks of Firash and Acknowledgment of Paternity
Explains the ruling on a master's acknowledgment of paternity and the four ranks of firash

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four ranks of firash and explain their effect on paternity establishment, and apply the Hanafi rule that the child is attributed to the nearest possible time.

Core Idea
The strength of a marital or ownership bond determines how paternity is established, negated, or protected.

This passage addresses the scenario where a master acknowledges a child in his slave woman's womb. It introduces the key concept of 'firash' (the legal bond creating a presumption of paternity) and classifies it into four ranks based on strength. Understanding these ranks is essential for correctly applying the rules of lineage, as the strength of the bond dictates whether paternity is automatic, requires a claim, or is immune to denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage dealing with a master saying 'If there is in your womb a child, then it is from me.' Note the role of witness testimony and the principle of attributing to the nearest possible time.
The child is not automatically his; it is attributed to the nearest possible time after purchase.
2
Understand the four ranks of firash
From 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar', the passage lists four ranks: weak (slave woman), medium (umm al-walad), strong (married woman/revocable 'iddah), and strongest (irrevocable 'iddah). Memorize the ruling for each.
Paternity moves from requiring a claim to being automatic and then becoming immune to negation.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on unconditional acknowledgment
The passage presents a difference: some say unconditional acknowledgment establishes lineage for two years, while al-Nahr restricts it to six months. Identify which position is mufta bihi and why.
The restriction to six months is based on the principle of nearest possible time.
4
Apply to conditional vs. unconditional
Note that the mufta bihi position makes no difference between conditional and unconditional acknowledgment; both require birth within six months for umm al-walad status.
This resolves potential confusion.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Combine the principles: the child is attributed to nearest time, the firash rank determines the procedure, and the time limit for acknowledgment is six months unless the master explicitly denies within two years in the minority view.
The school's authoritative position is the six-month restriction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال: لأمته إن كان في بطنك ولد، فهو منّى، فشهدت على الولادة امرأة فيضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات، فلا يلزم بلا دعوة. [1] قوله: إلى أقرب الأوقات؛ وهو هاهنا ما بعد الشراء، وذلك لما تقرر في مقره أن ما حدث ولم يعلم وقت حدوثه ينسب إلى أقرب الأوقات التي يمكن وجوده فيها. [2] قوله: فلا يلزم بلا دعوة؛ ذكر في «الدر المختار» وغيره: إن الفراش على أربع مراتب: 1. ضعيف، وهو فراش الأمة لا يثبت النسب فيه إلا بدعوة المولى. 2. ومتوسط: وهو فراش أمّ الولد فإنه يثبت فيه بلا دعوة، لكنه ينتفي بالنفي. 3. وقوي: وهو فراش المنكوحة، ومعتدة الرجعي، فإنه فيه لا ينتفي إلا باللعان. 4. وأقوى: كفراش معتدة البائن، فإن الولد لا ينتفي فيه أصلاً؛ لأن نفيه متوقف على اللعان، وشرط اللعان الزوجية. [3] قوله: إن كان ... الخ؛ ذكره بصورة التعليق ولو لم يعلّق، بل قال: هذا الحملُ مني، اختلفت فيه عبارات الكتب: ففي «غاية البيان»: إنه يثبت فيه نسبه إلى سنتين، حتى ينفيه، وذكر في «النهر» نقلاً عن «المحيط»: إنه ينبغي أن يقيد ذلك لما إذا وضعته لأقل من نصف حول من وقت الاعتراف، فلو لأكثر لا تصير أم ولد، وعلى هذا لا فرق بين صورة التعليق وبين غيرها. فإن في صورة التعليق أيضاً إنما تصير أم ولد إذا ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار، ولا إذا ولدت لستة أشهر أو أكثر، فلا يلزمه الولد؛ لأنه يحتمل أن تكون ...
And whoever says to his slave woman: 'If there is in your womb a child, then it is from me,' and a woman testifies to the birth, then it is attributed to the nearest time, so it is not incumbent without a claim. [1] His saying: to the nearest time; which here is after the purchase, because it has been established in its place that what occurs and its time of occurrence is unknown is attributed to the nearest times in which it could possibly exist. [2] His saying: so it is not incumbent without a claim; mentioned in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others: indeed the bed (firash) is of four ranks: 1. Weak: the bed of the slave woman, lineage is not established in it except by the master's claim. 2. Medium: the bed of umm al-walad, it is established without claim but it is negated by denial. 3. Strong: the bed of a married woman and the 'iddah of revocable divorce, it is not negated except by li'an. 4. Strongest: like the bed of the 'iddah of irrevocable divorce, the child is never negated; because its negation depends on li'an, and the condition of li'an is marriage. [3] His saying: 'if there is...' etc.; he mentioned it in the form of a condition, and if he did not condition but said: 'this pregnancy is from me,' the expressions in the books differ: in Ghayat al-Bayan: his lineage is established up to two years until he denies it; and it is mentioned in al-Nahr quoting from al-Muhit: it should be restricted to when she gives birth within less than half a year from the time of acknowledgment, for if more, she does not become umm al-walad, and on this there is no difference between the conditional form and otherwise. For in the conditional form too, she only becomes umm al-walad if she gives birth at less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, and not if she gives birth at six months or more, so the child is not incumbent upon him; because it is possible that...
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a master acknowledges a child in his slave woman's womb, and a woman testifies to the birth. The child is attributed to the nearest possible time (here after the purchase), so the child is not automatically incumbent upon him without a claim; the master must claim paternity. The commentary then explains the four ranks of 'firash' (the marital or ownership bond) as classified in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. These ranks determine the strength of paternity establishment: (1) Weak: a slave woman's child requires the master's claim. (2) Medium: umm al-walad's child is established without claim but can be negated by denial. (3) Strong: a married woman's child is not negated except by li'an. (4) Strongest: an irrevocable divorcee's child is never negated. The passage also discusses the difference between a conditional and unconditional acknowledgment. According to some authorities, if the master says 'this pregnancy is from me,' the lineage is established up to two years, but others restrict it to within six months of the acknowledgment. The school's relied-upon position is that umm al-walad status is only confirmed if the child is born within six months of the acknowledgment; otherwise, it is not established. This illustrates the meticulousness of Hanafi jurists in balancing the presumption of paternity with the possibility of false claims.

Key Terms
الفراش (al-firāsh): The legal bond (marriage or ownership) that creates a presumption of paternity.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has borne a child recognized by the master; she has special status and her child is free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which type of firash requires the master's claim (da'wa) to establish lineage?
A) The weak firash (slave woman)
B) The medium firash (umm al-walad)
C) The strong firash (married woman)
D) The strongest firash (irrevocable divorcee)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of firash into four ranks provides a nuanced framework for determining paternity based on the strength of the legal bond.

Conditional Paternity Declaration for a Slave-Girl's Child
Explains the ruling on conditional paternity claim for an unborn child of a slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master's conditional paternity declaration to his slave-girl and identify the requirements (explicit claim and birth within six months) for the child to be established as his offspring.

Core Idea
A slave-girl's child is not automatically linked to the master; an explicit claim is required due to weak firash.

This passage from al-Wiqayah, commented upon in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, addresses a specific scenario: a master tells his slave-girl that if she bears a child, it is from him. You might think this automatically makes the child free and establishes paternity, but Hanafi law imposes an additional condition—an explicit claim after birth. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling, including the principle of attributing events to the nearest possible time and the hierarchy of firash (legal bed) that determines the strength of lineage establishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
The act is a master's conditional statement to his slave-girl: 'If there is a child in your womb, it is from me.' The initial ruling is that the child is attributed to the nearest possible time of conception (here, post-purchase), but this does not make the child legally his master's son.
The phrase 'fala yalzam bi la da'wa' is key: it does not become binding without a claim.
2
Understand the principle of attributing to the nearest time
The commentary explains that when the time of an event is unknown, it is attributed to the earliest possible moment. Here, that is after the purchase of the slave-girl. This is a usul principle applied to lineage cases.
This principle appears in other fiqh areas, such as unknown dates of contracts.
3
Recognize the need for a claim (da'wa) due to weak firash
The slave-girl's firash is classified as 'weak' in the Hanafi hierarchy. Lineage from a weak firash is not established without the master's explicit claim. The commentary lists the four firash levels: weak (slave-girl), intermediate (umm walad), strong (married woman), strongest (woman in irrevocable divorce).
For a wife (strong firash), lineage is established automatically and can only be negated by li'an.
4
Apply the time limit for birth after declaration
The text notes a dispute about the time limit for the birth to be attributed to the master. The relied-upon view is that if the birth occurs within six months of the declaration (whether conditional or unconditional), the child is his and she becomes umm walad. If beyond six months, the child is not binding because conception could have occurred after the statement.
Some scholars (e.g., Ghayat al-Bayan) suggest a two-year limit, but the later authorities prefer six months.
5
Synthesize the full legal rule
Combining the above: For the child to be established as the master's offspring and for the mother to become umm walad, two conditions must be met: (1) the master makes an explicit claim after birth, and (2) the birth occurs within six months of the declaration. Without these, the child is attributed to the nearest time (post-purchase) but not linked to the master.
This ruling applies to both conditional and unconditional declarations, as clarified in al-Inayah and other works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال : لأمته إن كان في بطنك ولد ، فهو منّى ، فشهدت على الولادة امرأة فيضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات، فلا يلزم بلا دعوة. [١] قوله : إلى أقرب الأوقات ؛ وهو هاهنا ما بعد الشراء، وذلك لما تقرر في مقره أن ما حدث ولم يعلم وقت حدوثه ينسب إلى أقرب الأوقات التي يمكن وجوده فيها. [٢] قوله : فلا يلزم بلا دعوة ؛ ذكر في «الدر المختار» وغيره : إن الفراش على أربع مراتب : ١. ضعيف، وهو فراشُ الأمة لا يثبتُ النسب فيه إلا بدعوة المولى. ٢. ومتوسط : وهو فراش أمّ الولد فإنّه يثبت فيه بلا دعوة، لكنه ينتفي بالنفي. ٣. وقوي : وهو فراش المنكوحة، ومعتدة الرجعي، فإنّه فيه لا ينتفي إلا باللعان. ٤. وأقوى : كفراش معتدة البائن، فإنّ الولد لا ينتفي فيه أصلاً ؛ لأن نفيه متوقف على اللعان، وشرط اللعان الزوجية. [٣]قوله : إن كان ...الخ ؛ ذكره بصورة التعليق ولو لم يعلّق ، بل قال : هذا الحملُ مني، اختلفت فيه عبارات الكتب : ففي غاية البيان»: إنّه يثبت فيه نسبه إلى سنتين ، حتى ينفيه، وذكر في «النهر» نقلا عن «المحيط»: إنّه ينبغي أن يقيد ذلك لما إذا وضعته لأقل من نصف حول من وقت الاعتراف، فلو لاكثر لا تصير أم ولد، وعلى هذا لا فرق بين صورة التعليق وبين غيرها. فإن في صورة التعليق أيضاً إنّما تصير أم ولد إذا ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار، ولا إذا ولدت لستة أشهر أو أكثر ، فلا يلزمه الولد ؛ لأنه يحتمل أن تكون حملت بعد مقالة المولى. كذا في «العناية» و«الفتح» و«البحر و«النهر) وفي صورة ستة أشهر تأمل.
And whoever said to his slave-girl: 'If there is a child in your womb, it is from me,' and a woman witnessed the birth, it is attributed to the nearest of times, so it does not become necessary without a claim. [1] His statement: 'to the nearest of times' – and here it is the time after the purchase, according to what is established in its place that what occurs and whose time of occurrence is not known is attributed to the nearest time in which it could have existed. [2] His statement: 'so it does not become necessary without a claim' – It is mentioned in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others: The bedding (firash) is of four ranks: 1. Weak: the bedding of a slave-girl – lineage is not established through it except with the master's claim. 2. Intermediate: the bedding of a mother of a child (umm walad) – lineage is established through it without a claim, but it can be negated by denial. 3. Strong: the bedding of a married woman and a woman in a revocable divorce – lineage cannot be negated except by mutual imprecation (li'an). 4. Strongest: such as the bedding of a woman in an irrevocable divorce – lineage cannot be negated at all because its negation depends on li'an, and the condition for li'an is marital relationship. [3] His statement: 'if there is...' – he mentioned it in the form of a condition; if he had not conditioned and said: 'this pregnancy is from me,' the expressions of the books differ: In Ghayat al-Bayan: 'lineage is established through it for up to two years, until he denies it.' And it is mentioned in al-Nahr, quoting from al-Muhit: 'It should be restricted to when she gives birth within less than half a year from the time of confession; if more, she does not become umm walad. On this basis, there is no difference between the case of condition and other cases. For in the case of condition, she only becomes umm walad if she gives birth within less than six months from the time of declaration, and not if she gives birth at six months or more, so the child does not become binding upon him because it is possible that she conceived after the master's statement.' Thus in al-Inayah, al-Fath, al-Bahr, and al-Nahr. And the case of six months is questionable.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Wiqayah, commented upon in 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. It addresses the legal effect of a master's conditional declaration to his slave-girl that any child in her womb is from him, combined with a woman's testimony of the birth. The core ruling is that the child is attributed to the nearest possible time of conception (aqrab al-awaqit), which in this context is the time after the master purchased the slave-girl. However, this attribution does not automatically establish legal paternity or make the child free (umm walad) without an explicit claim (da'wa) from the master. The commentary clarifies the principle of attributing uncertain events to the nearest possible time, a key usul al-fiqh principle. Then it explains the different levels of 'firash' (the marital or concubine bed) from the Hanafi school, showing that for a slave-girl (not umm walad), the firash is weak, so paternity is not established merely by the master's conditional statement; he must actively claim the child. For umm walad, it is intermediate, etc. The commentary also resolves a potential confusion: even if the master made the declaration unconditionally (e.g., 'this pregnancy is from me'), there is a difference of opinion. The relied-upon view is that paternity is established only if she gives birth within six months of the declaration (the minimum period of pregnancy), otherwise it might have been conceived later. The same applies to the conditional declaration. Thus, the ruling emphasizes that a mere conditional statement does not suffice; a claim and timely birth are needed.

Key Terms
فراش (firash): The legal relationship (bed) that serves as a basis for establishing lineage; for a slave-girl it is weak, for a wife it is strong.
دعوة (da'wa): An explicit claim by the master that the child is his, required to establish paternity for a slave-girl's child.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who has borne a child to her master; upon the master's death she becomes free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a master's conditional declaration to his slave-girl not automatically establish paternity?
A) The declaration was conditional, so it is invalid until the condition (birth) occurs.
B) The slave-girl's firash is weak, requiring an explicit claim after birth.
C) The woman's testimony of birth is unreliable.
D) The child must first be attributed to the nearest time, which could be after purchase.

Key Takeaway
A slave-girl's child is only linked to the master through an explicit claim; a mere conditional declaration does not suffice, even if the birth occurs within six months.

Conditions for Valid Paternity Declaration and Umm Walad Claim
Conditions for paternity declaration and umm walad claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid paternity declaration and explain how the mother's claim establishes umm walad status.

Core Idea
A man's paternity claim for a known child is valid only if the child is of possible age, has no known lineage, and does not deny it.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a man declares an existing child as his son, then dies. The child's mother then claims she is the umm walad of the deceased. The text establishes that the paternity declaration is valid under three conditions, and the mother's statement suffices to identify the child, making her an umm walad with associated rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal scenario
Recognize the situation: a man says 'he is my son' regarding an existing child, then dies. The mother then claims to be the umm walad.
This is not a case of a child born in marriage, but a voluntary acknowledgment.
2
Extract the three conditions
From the commentary, list the three conditions that must be met for the declaration to be valid: (1) biological possibility, (2) no known lineage, (3) no denial by the child.
Each condition prevents fraudulent claims.
3
Understand the role of the mother's statement
The mother's claim that the child is his and she is his wife is sufficient to identify the child. It does not require additional witnesses.
The mother must be known as the mother of the child.
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Test the conditions by applying them to a hypothetical. Check each condition and conclude validity.
If any condition is missing, the declaration is void.

Or regarding a child: 'He is my son,' and he died, and the mother of the child said, 'She is the mother of his child.' [1] His statement: 'She is the mother of his child' – meaning the lineage of that child is established from him, and his mother becomes an umm walad for her master, because the cause for establishing lineage, which is the claim (da'wa), was found from the master by his saying 'He is from me,' and the only need is to identify the child, so the statement of one woman suffices. [2] His statement: 'Or regarding a child' – it is restricted by conditions: First: that the child be of the kind who can be born from one like him; if not, such as being equal in age to the declarant or older, or younger to an extent that he cannot be his child, then the declarant's statement is disregarded due to obvious intellectual falsehood. Second: that he not be of known lineage; if his lineage is known from someone, the declarant's statement is not considered. Third: that the child does not deny him. [3] His statement: 'and the mother of the child said' – meaning the woman who is known to be the mother of that child said: 'He is his son and I am the wife of that deceased declarant.' And it is conditioned that she be known as the mother of that child because if she were not, she would not inherit, due to the lack of the necessity of establishing her marital relationship by the establishment of the child's sonship.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn covering a second scenario: a man declares that a specific existing child is his son, then dies. Subsequently, the child's mother claims that she is the umm walad of the deceased, i.e., the mother of his child. The commentary explains that the child's lineage is established from the man because he made a claim (da'wa). The mother's statement suffices to identify the child, so she becomes umm walad. However, the commentary then sets three conditions for the paternity declaration to be valid: (1) The child must be biologically possible given the ages – it cannot be older or impossibly young. (2) The child must not already have a known lineage to another man. (3) The child must not deny the paternity, i.e., the child must affirm or at least not contradict the man's statement. The mother's claim that she is the wife of the declarant is also examined; she must be known as the mother of the child for her inheritance to depend on the established marriage. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that a man can voluntarily establish paternity for a child not previously attributed to him, subject to these conditions to prevent fraud.

Key Terms
دعوة (da'wa): The claim made by the man that the child is his, which serves as the cause for establishing paternity.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who bears a child to her master; here, the mother of the child claims this status after the man's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child must be of an age that makes paternity biologically possible.
B) The child must not be of known lineage from another.
C) The child must explicitly consent to the declaration.
D) The child must not deny the declaration.

Key Takeaway
A man's paternity declaration for a known child is valid only if the child is of possible age, has no known lineage, and does not deny it; the mother's claim then establishes her as umm walad.

Acknowledgment of Paternity: Conditions and Inheritance Effects
Rulings on acknowledgment of paternity and its effects on inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid acknowledgment of paternity and explain when the child's mother inherits as a wife.

Core Idea
A man's acknowledgment of paternity establishes lineage only if the child could be his offspring and no contradiction arises.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the Hanafi rules on establishing paternity through a man's acknowledgment (iqrar). It lays out strict conditions to prevent false claims, and then addresses inheritance rights for the mother. Understanding these conditions is essential for applying inheritance law correctly, especially when the mother claims to be the deceased's wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two cases: (1) a master acknowledges a child from his slave woman, making her umm walad; (2) a man acknowledges a free child as his son, and the child's mother claims to be his wife.
2
List the conditions for valid acknowledgment
For acknowledgment to be valid, the child must be of an age that could be his offspring (not older or too young), must not be of known lineage, and must not deny the claim. Also, the child's mother must be known to be free and Muslim for inheritance.
These conditions prevent abuse of the iqrar mechanism.
3
Analyze the role of valid marriage
The commentary emphasizes that for the mother to inherit as a wife, the child's paternity must be presumed from a valid marriage (nikah sahih), not from fornication or invalid marriage. This presumption is the 'basis for permissibility'.
This is a key Hanafi principle: lineage is attributed to valid marriage unless proven otherwise.
4
Apply the ruling to inheritance
If the conditions are met, the child inherits as a son. The mother inherits as a wife only if she is known to be free, Muslim, and the child's paternity is through valid marriage. Her mere claim is not sufficient.
The cross-madhhab difference: Shafi'is may accept the acknowledgment alone for inheritance, while Hanafis require separate proof of marriage.

Likewise in al-'Inayah and al-Fath and al-Bahr and al-Nahr, and in the case of six months, consider. [1] His saying: 'So she is umm walad' means the lineage of that child is established from him, and his mother becomes umm walad for her master; because the cause of establishing lineage, which is the claim, existed from the master by his saying 'He is from me', and there is only need to identify the child, so one woman's statement suffices. [2] His saying: 'Or for a child' is restricted by conditions: First: that the child be of such a type that one like him could be born to one like him; if not, such as he is equal in age to the affirmant or older or younger to an extent that it is impossible for him to be his child, then the affirmant's statement is disregarded due to apparent intellectual falsehood. Second: that he not be of known lineage; if his lineage is known from someone, the affirmant's statement is not considered. Third: that the child does not deny him. [3] His saying: 'And the mother of the child said' means the woman who is known to be the mother of that child said: 'He is his son and I am the wife of that deceased affirmant'; and it is restricted to her being known as mother of that child because if she were not, she would not inherit due to lack of necessary proof of her marriage due to proof of the child's sonship. (1) Because lineage is established by claim, and birth is established by the midwife's testimony; this is if she gives birth less than six months from the time of the acknowledgment because we are certain of his existence at that time; if she gives birth after more than that, it does not oblige him due to possibility of conception after that. See: Sharh Ibn Malik (q1/118). (2) Al-'Inayah (4:365). (3) Fath al-Qadir (4:366). (4) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (4:180). (5) Al-Nahr al-Fa'iq (2:498). [Page 522] 522 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah. 'He is his son and I am his wife,' they both inherit. And if the heir says: You are his umm walad, and her free status is unknown, she does not inherit. Regarding 'He is his son and I am his wife, they both inherit': meaning the child and his mother inherit from the affirmant; because if the woman is known to be free and known to be the mother of the child, then there is no way to establish the child's sonship to him except through a valid marriage to his mother; because that is the basis for permissibility (3)(1). (And if his heir says: You are his umm walad, and her free status is unknown, she does not inherit): meaning the mother of the child, (2) and the child inherits (2). The ruling is also restricted to her being Muslim, and known to be free; because if her Islam is not known, she does not inherit, as there is no marriage between a disbeliever and a Muslim, and likewise if she is not known to be free; due to the possibility that she is his umm walad, and inheritance is only among the specificities of marriage. [1] His saying: 'He is his son' is needed even though sonship is established by the deceased's acknowledgment; because if she said: 'I am his wife and this is my son from another man,' she would be denying what she used to establish her marriage, which is his saying 'This is my son,' so she does not inherit. [2] His saying: 'They both inherit' because since his sonship was established by the deceased's acknowledgment and she is known to be his mother, then necessarily she must be his wife, so her statement is accepted without proof. [3] His saying: 'Because it is the basis for permissibility' refers to refuting what might be said: That lineage is established by valid marriage as well as by invalid marriage, by intercourse with a legal ambiguity, and by right hand possession, so his sonship of that child does not necessitate the mother's marriage such that her inheritance is established. The gist of the refutation is that the basis for permissibility is marriage, nothing else, so it is attributed to it. [4] His saying: 'And if...' etc. means if that woman is not known to be free and the heirs of the deceased affirmant say: 'You are umm walad of our testator who affirmed the sonship of that child,' she does not inherit from him unless she proves with complete evidence that she is his wife. (1) i.e., valid marriage, which is the considered basis for lineage; thus upon his acknowledgment of sonship, it is attributed to it unless the opposite appears, just as it is attributed to it when he denies his known son, so the denier is obligated with hadd and li'an, and the possibility of attaching it to others by invalid marriage or intercourse with ambiguity is not considered. Its completion is in al-Tabyin (3:47). (2) Because the appearance of freedom by virtue of the abode is evidence for removing slavery, not for eligibility of inheritance. See: Durar al-Hukkam (2:1).
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary expanding on rulings from the matn regarding the establishment of lineage (nasab) through a man's acknowledgment (iqrar) that a child is his son. The passage covers two main scenarios: (1) when a master says to his slave woman's child 'he is my son,' making the woman an umm walad; (2) when a man says to a child (who may be free) 'he is my son' and dies, and the child's mother claims that she is his wife, leading to inheritance. The commentary specifies conditions for the acknowledgment to be valid: the child must be of an age that could be his offspring, not of known lineage, and not deny him. For inheritance, the mother must be known to be free, Muslim, and the child's sonship is presumed to arise from a valid marriage (nikah sahih), not from fornication or invalid marriage, because valid marriage is the 'basis for permissibility' (al-mawdu' li al-hall). This presumption is crucial for her to inherit as a wife. The commentary also addresses a potential objection that lineage can be established through other means, but clarifies that inheritance requires the valid marriage link. The author follows the order of the original text, explaining each phrase.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child from her master, thereby gaining the status where she becomes free upon her master's death and her child is free.
إقرار (iqrar): A legal acknowledgment or admission, here of paternity, which establishes lineage under certain conditions.
نكاح صحيح (nikah sahih): A valid marriage contract fulfilling all legal conditions, which is the presumed cause for establishing lineage in such cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for a mother to inherit from a man who acknowledged paternity of her child?
A) She must be known to be free and Muslim, and the child's paternity must be proven through a valid marriage.
B) She only needs to prove that the child is from him, regardless of marriage.
C) She must be a free woman, but her religion does not matter.
D) She must have been his slave woman who bore his child.

Key Takeaway
Acknowledgment of paternity establishes lineage but does not automatically make the mother a wife for inheritance; she must prove valid marriage.

Inheritance When Mother's Free Status Unknown
Ruling on mother's inheritance when her free status is unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for a mother to inherit from her child's father when her free status is unknown, and distinguish between presumption of freedom for personal status and for inheritance.

Core Idea
Presumption of freedom does not establish inheritance; proven marriage is required.

This lesson examines a specific inheritance scenario: a woman whose free status is unknown claims inheritance from a man who acknowledged paternity of her child. The commentator clarifies that the mere fact that she lives in a Muslim land does not suffice to prove her freedom for inheritance purposes. She must present conclusive evidence of a valid marriage. We will unpack the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key question
What is the legal issue when a woman's free status is unknown and she seeks inheritance? The deceased acknowledged paternity of her child, but her freedom is not established.
Focus on the condition of freedom, not the marriage itself.
2
Determine the ruling
The Hanafi ruling: she does not inherit unless she proves valid marriage with complete evidence. The commentator explicitly states this.
Note the phrase 'لا ترث منه إلا إذا أثبتت بحجة تامة'.
3
Understand the rationale
Why is apparent freedom from living in dar al-Islam not enough? Because 'ظهور الحرية باعتبار الدار حجة في رفع الرق لا في استحقاق الإرث' – it is evidence for removing slavery, not for earning inheritance.
Inheritance requires a definite legal tie (valid marriage), not a presumption.
4
Distinguish from other contexts
In matters like personal status, presumption of freedom suffices. But inheritance is a specific financial right that demands proof. This distinction is key.
This explains why the Hanafi school treats inheritance differently from slavery-related rulings.

(١) أي النكاح الصحيح، وهو المعتبر الموضوع للنسب فعند إقراره بالبنوة يحمل عليه ما لم يظهر خلاف ذلك، كما يحمل عليه عند نفيه عن ابنه المعروف حتى وجب على النافي الحد واللعن ، ولم يعتبر احتمال إلحاقه بغيره بالنكاح الفاسد أو الوطء بالشبهة. وتمامه في «التبيين»(٣: ٤٧). (۲) لأن ظهور الحرية باعتبار الدار حجة في رفع الرق لا في استحقاق الإرث. ينظر : درر الحكام .(2) : 1)
[4] His saying: 'And if...' etc. means if that woman is not known to be free and the heirs of the deceased affirmant say: 'You are umm walad of our testator who affirmed the sonship of that child,' she does not inherit from him unless she proves with complete evidence that she is his wife. (1) i.e., valid marriage, which is the considered basis for lineage; thus upon his acknowledgment of sonship, it is attributed to it unless the opposite appears, just as it is attributed to it when he denies his known son, so the denier is obligated with hadd and li'an, and the possibility of attaching it to others by invalid marriage or intercourse with ambiguity is not considered. Its completion is in al-Tabyin (3:47). (2) Because the appearance of freedom by virtue of the abode is evidence for removing slavery, not for eligibility of inheritance. See: Durar al-Hukkam (2:1).
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's phrase 'and if the heir says: You are his umm walad, and her free status is unknown, she does not inherit.' The commentator explains that when a woman's free status is not known, she cannot inherit from the deceased who acknowledged paternity of her child unless she proves with conclusive evidence that she was his wife in a valid marriage. The reason is that mere acknowledgment of paternity does not automatically prove marriage; for inheritance, marriage must be established. The commentator adds that apparent freedom based on living in a Muslim land (dar al-Islam) is sufficient to presume freedom for most purposes, but not for claiming inheritance, because inheritance is based on specific legal ties (marriage). The text also reiterates that valid marriage is the only proper basis for paternity, excluding invalid marriage or intercourse with ambiguity.

Key Terms
حرية (hurriyyah): Free status; the woman must be known to be free for inheritance claims.
إرث (irth): Inheritance; here the right to inherit from the deceased based on marriage relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does a woman whose free status is unknown not inherit from a man who acknowledged paternity of her child?
A) Because she might be a slave, and slaves do not inherit.
B) Because inheritance requires proven marriage, and unknown free status leaves doubt.
C) Because she must be a Muslim to inherit.
D) Because the child's paternity is not established.

Key Takeaway
A woman whose free status is unknown must prove a valid marriage to inherit, even if the deceased acknowledged her child's paternity.

Order of Custody for Female Relatives
Expands the Hanafi order of female custody with conditions and an internal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of female relatives entitled to custody and identify the conditions (freedom, religion) that affect eligibility.

Core Idea
Custody follows the mother's line: maternal grandmother, paternal grandmother, sisters, then maternal aunts before paternal aunts.

Custody (hadana) is a right primarily vested in the mother and then in female relatives in a specific order. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi sequence, its basis in maternal kinship, and the conditions that must be met for a woman to be eligible. You will learn not only the order but also the rationale behind it and a key internal dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling category
Determine the legal nature of custody: it is a right (mubah) that the mother and female relatives can claim, not an obligation.
2
Trace the order after the mother
List the sequence: maternal grandmother (even high), paternal grandmother, full sister, uterine sister, consanguine sister, maternal aunt (full, uterine, consanguine), paternal aunt (same order), then further female relatives.
The order is based on proximity of maternal kinship.
3
Apply the condition of freedom
All eligible women must be free. A slave woman or umm walad is disqualified because she is occupied with her master's service. Exception: if the child is a slave, the master has priority.
A mukataba who gives birth after kitaba has more right to her child.
4
Apply the condition of religion
A dhimmi (non-Muslim) mother retains custody of her child from a Muslim husband until the child can understand religious differences. This is because compassion does not depend on religion.
If both parents are dhimmis, this condition does not apply.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars give the maternal aunt priority over the paternal half-sister based on the hadith 'al-khala walida', while others favor the paternal half-sister due to greater compassion. The relied-upon order places the maternal aunt after the sisters.
This dispute shows how different proofs (hadith vs. general consideration) lead to different tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمَّ لأمها وإن عَلَت، ثُمَّ لأم أبيه، ثُمَّ لأختِه لأب وأم، ثُمَّ لام، ثم لأب، ثُمَّ لخالته كذلك) : أي لأب وأمّ، ثُمَّ لأم، ثُمَّ لأب، فإن الخالة أخت الأم، فأختها لأب وأم أولَى، ثُمَّ أُختها لأم، ثُمَّ لأب، وذلك لأن الأصل في هذا الباب الأم ... ثم لأمها؛ أي لأم الأم، ثم لأم أم الأم، وهكذا. قوله: وإن علت؛ وأما أم أبي الأم، فهي متأخرة عن أم الأب، بل عن الخالة أيضاً كما في «البحر». قوله: ثم لأم أبيه؛ هذا الضمير، وكذا الضمائر الآتية كلها ترجع إلى الطفل، ولذا ذكر لفظ الطفل في المسألة السابقة، وإلا فتلك المسألة تتصوّر في البالغ أيضاً. قوله: ثم لأخته لأب وأم؛ أي إن لم يكن من تقدم فحق الحضانة لأخت الصغير، وتقدم أخته لأبوين؛ أي العينية؛ لترجحها على غيرها، وقوة قرابتها، ثم أخته أي الأخيافية، ثم لأب؛ أي العلائية، وإنما قدمت لام؛ لأن هذا الحق لقرابته الأم. قوله: ثم لخالته؛ ذكر الزيلعي وغيره أن بعد الأخوات الحق لبنت الأخت لأبوين، ثم بنت الأخت لأم ثم الخالة، وبنت الأخت لأب مؤخرة عن الخالة على الصحيح، وبعدها الحق لبنات الأخ لأب وأم، ثم لأم، ثم لأب، وبعد ذلك الحق ثم عمته كذلك، بشرط حريتهن، فلا حق لأمة، وأم ولد فيه، والدمية كالمسلمة حتى يعقل ديناً فالقرابة من جهتها قدمت على القرابة من طرف الأب، (ثُمَّ عمته كذلك) : أي لأب وأم، ثُمَّ لأمّ، ثُمَّ لأب، فإنَّ العمَّةَ أختُ الأب، فتقدَّمُ أختُهُ لأب وأم، ثُمَّ لأم، ثُمَّ لأب. (بشرط حريتهن، فلا حَقٌّ لأمة، وأُمِّ ولد فيه) : أي في الولد. (والدمية كالمسلمة حتى يعقل ديناً) : أي في ولد المسلم للعمات، ثم خالة الأم، ثم خالة الأب، ثم عمات الأمهات والآباء، وبعد ذلك الحق للعصبات على ما سيأتي. قوله: فالقرابة من جهتها قدمت؛ ولذلك قدم بعضهم الخالة على الأخت لأب، ويؤيده حديث: «الخالة والدة»، أخرجه أبو داود وغيره، ومن قدم الأخت لأب نظر إلى وفور الشفقة. قوله: بشرط حريتهن؛ أي المذكورات؛ وذلك لأن غير الحرة مشتغلة بخدمة مولاها، فلا تقدر على تربية الولد، وذكر في «المجتبى» وغيره: إن الولد إن كان رقيقاً كان أحق به؛ لأنه للمولى، وكذا ولد المكابتة التي ولدت بعد الكتابة هي أحق بها؛ لأنه داخل تحت الكتابة. كذا في «الفتح». قوله: وأم ولد فيه؛ أي إذا طلقها زوجها، أما إذا أعتقها المولى فهي بمنزلة المطلقة الحرة. قوله: والذمية؛ يعني إذا كانت الأم مثلاً ذمية يهودية أو نصرانية تحت مسلم، فلها أيضاً حق التربية؛ لأن الشفقة لا تختلف باختلاف الدين. قوله: أي في ولد المسلم؛ يعني هذه الغاية اعتبارها إنما هو في ولد الزوج المسلم، وأما إذا كان الزوجان ذميين فلا يحتاج إليها.
Then for her mother even if high, then for the mother of his father, then for his sister from father and mother, then for his maternal aunt similarly: that is, from father and mother, then from mother, then from father, for the maternal aunt is the sister of the mother, so her sister from father and mother is first, then her sister from mother, then from father, and that is because the basis in this chapter is the mother... Then for her mother: meaning the mother of the mother, then the mother of the mother of the mother, and so on. His statement: 'even if high' – as for the mother of the father's mother, she is after the father's mother, rather after the maternal aunt as well, as in al-Bahr. His statement: 'then for the mother of his father' – this pronoun, and all the following pronouns, refer to the child, hence the word 'child' was mentioned in the previous issue; otherwise that issue also applies to an adult. His statement: 'then for his sister from father and mother' – meaning if there is none of those who preceded, then the right of custody is for the sister of the young child, and his sister from both parents is preferred due to her precedence and strength of relation, then his sister (i.e., the uterine sister), then from father (i.e., the consanguine sister); the uterine sister is given precedence because this right belongs to the maternal kinship. His statement: 'then for his maternal aunt' – al-Zayla'i and others mentioned that after the sisters, the right is for the daughter of the sister from both parents, then the daughter of the sister from mother, then the maternal aunt, and the daughter of the sister from father is after the maternal aunt according to the correct view, and after that the right is for the daughters of the brother from father and mother, then from mother, then from father, and after that the right is then for his paternal aunt similarly, with the condition that they be free, so there is no right for a slave woman or umm walad in it, and the dhimmi woman is like the Muslim woman until the child understands religion; thus kinship from her side is given precedence over kinship from the father's side. (Then for his paternal aunt similarly): that is, from father and mother, then from mother, then from father, for the paternal aunt is the sister of the father, so his sister from father and mother is given precedence, then from mother, then from father. (With the condition that they be free, so there is no right for a slave woman or umm walad in it): that is, regarding the child. (And the dhimmi woman is like the Muslim woman until the child understands religion): that is, regarding the child of the Muslim man, for the paternal aunts, then the maternal aunt of the mother, then the maternal aunt of the father, then the paternal aunts of mothers and fathers, and after that the right is for the agnatic relatives (asaba) as will come. His statement: 'Thus the kinship from her side is given precedence' – therefore some scholars gave precedence to the maternal aunt over the paternal sister, supported by the hadith: 'The maternal aunt is like a mother,' reported by Abu Dawud and others, while those who gave precedence to the paternal sister considered abundant compassion. His statement: 'with the condition that they be free' – meaning those mentioned; because the non-free are occupied with serving their master and cannot raise the child. It is mentioned in al-Mujtaba and others: if the child is a slave, the master has more right to him; similarly, the child of a mukataba who gave birth after the kitaba is more entitled to her because she is included in the kitaba, as in al-Fath. His statement: 'and umm walad in it' – meaning if her husband divorces her; but if the master frees her, she is like a free divorced woman. His statement: 'and the dhimmi woman' – meaning if the mother, for instance, is a dhimmi, Jewish or Christian, married to a Muslim, she also has the right to raise the child because compassion does not differ due to difference of religion. His statement: 'that is, regarding the child of the Muslim' – meaning this consideration applies only to the child of the Muslim husband; if both spouses are dhimmis, it is not needed.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the order of female relatives entitled to custody (hadana) in Hanafi fiqh. The author, commenting on the base text (matn), details the sequence after the mother. First, the maternal grandmother, even if high (mother's mother, then her mother, etc.), second the paternal grandmother, third the full sister (both parents), fourth the uterine sister, fifth the consanguine sister, sixth the maternal aunt (initially from both parents, then from mother, then from father). The commentary explains the reasoning: the basis is the mother's side, as custody is tied to maternal care. It also notes an internal dispute: some scholars prefer the maternal aunt over the paternal half-sister due to the hadith 'The maternal aunt is like a mother' (Sunan Abi Dawud), while others favor the paternal sister due to greater compassion. The text then continues with the order after the aunts: paternal aunts similarly, then the maternal aunt of the mother, then the maternal aunt of the father, then the paternal aunts of the mothers and fathers, followed by the agnatic relatives (asaba). A key condition is that all these must be free women; a slave woman (ama) or umm walad has no right to custody because they are occupied with their master's service. However, if the child is a slave, the master has priority. A mukataba who gives birth after the kitaba has more right to her child as the child falls under the kitaba. The passage also addresses the dhimmi mother: she retains custody of her child from a Muslim husband until the child can understand religious differences, because compassion is not affected by religion. If both parents are dhimmis, this condition does not apply.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadana): The right to physically care for and raise a child, including custody and upbringing.
خالة (khala): Maternal aunt; sister of the mother.
عمة (amma): Paternal aunt; sister of the father.
أمة (ama): A female slave; a slave woman.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, and is therefore freed upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is next in line for custody after the mother?
A) The paternal grandmother
B) The maternal grandmother
C) The full sister
D) The maternal aunt

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of female custody is: mother, maternal grandmother, paternal grandmother, full sister, uterine sister, consanguine sister, maternal aunt, paternal aunt, and so on, with the conditions that the custodian must be free and, if non-Muslim, may only retain custody until the child understands religion.

Custody of Female Relatives: Order and Condition of Freedom
Commentary on the order and conditions of female custody.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of female relatives entitled to custody and apply the condition of freedom to determine eligibility.

Core Idea
Only free women are entitled to custody; a slave woman or umm walad cannot care for the child due to servitude obligations.

In this passage, the commentator elaborates on the hierarchy of female custodians after the mother. The key principle is that all custodians must be free, and an intra-Hanafi dispute exists regarding precedence between the maternal aunt and the paternal sister, resolved by the hadith 'The maternal aunt is like a mother'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the order of female relatives
The text lists: mother's mother, father's mother, sisters (by same parents, then mother, then father), then paternal aunts (عمات) in the same order, then maternal aunts (خالات), etc. Note that the mother's side is generally preferred.
The full order includes maternal aunts of the mother, then of the father, then paternal aunts of mothers and fathers.
2
Apply the condition of freedom
All female custodians must be free (حرة). A slave woman (أمة) and an umm walad (unless manumitted) have no right because they are occupied with serving their master.
If the child is also a slave, the mother is more entitled because the child belongs to the master.
3
Examine the dispute: maternal aunt vs. paternal sister
Some scholars preferred the maternal aunt over the sister from father due to the hadith 'الخالة والدة' (the maternal aunt is like a mother). Others preferred the sister from father based on stronger compassion.
The dominant Hanafi view follows the hadith, giving precedence to the maternal aunt.
4
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon ruling is that free maternal relatives take precedence over paternal ones, and the maternal aunt is preferred over the sister from father.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and confirmed by later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Thus in al-Fath. (3) His statement: 'And an umm walad in it' i.e., if her husband divorces her, but if the master manumits her, she is like a free divorced woman. [4] His statement: 'And the dhimmi woman' means if the mother is, for example, a dhimmi Jew or Christian under a Muslim husband, she also has the right of upbringing because affection does not differ with difference of religion. [0] His statement: 'i.e., concerning the child of a Muslim' means this consideration of the end is only concerning the child of a Muslim husband; but if both spouses are dhimmis, there is no need for it. In al-Hidayah: as long as he does not understand religion, or it is feared that he may become accustomed to kufr. And his statement: 'or it is feared' must be in jussive case, i.e., yukhaf, because it is conjoined to 'ya'qil' which is jussive by lam; because the meaning is 'as long as it is not feared.' This condition is not mentioned in al-Wiqayah, and it must be observed, because becoming accustomed to kufr may occur before understanding religion. So if it is feared that he will become accustomed to kufr, he is taken away from her. [1] His statement: In al-Hidayah its wording is: 'Or the dhimmi woman is more entitled to her Muslim child as long as he does not understand religions or it is feared that he may become accustomed to kufr, due to consideration before that and possibility of harm after it.' [2] His statement: 'must be observed'... its gist: his statement 'yukhaf' is conjoined to 'ya'qil', which is jussive by lam, and the conjoined follows the conjoined in parsing, so it must be jussive, so the correct form is 'yukhaf'. The answer: it is possible that 'aw' means 'until' or 'unless', as in their saying: 'I will surely adhere to you or you give me my right', as mentioned in al-Nihayah and al-Binayah and others. So the insistence on making 'yukhaf' jussive as stated by the commentator is not appropriate, unless it is said that by 'obligatory' he means commendable. [3] His statement: 'This condition' means that the condition of absence of fear of becoming accustomed to kufr mentioned in al-Hidayah was not mentioned in the matn, and it must be mentioned, because the young child may not understand religion nor comprehend the beauties and detriments of religion, but one fears his becoming accustomed to kufr, such as his habit of going with disbelievers to their places of worship, prostrating to their false objects of worship, and similar actions. [4] His statement: 'he is taken away' i.e., he is removed from the custody of the guardian and placed with the Muslims. It is said in al-Fath: 'And she is prevented from feeding him wine and pork, and if feared, he is placed with a Muslim family.'
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the custody (hadanah) rights of female relatives. It begins by stating that paternal aunts (عمات) have custody rights in the same order as sisters but only if they are free. The condition of freedom is explained: an enslaved woman (أمة) and an umm walad (mother of a child from her master) have no right to custody because they are occupied with their master's service. However, if the child is also a slave, the mother is more entitled since the child belongs to the master. The commentary then discusses the dhimmi mother: she is like a Muslim mother in having custody of her child, as affection does not differ by religion. But the right is limited: until the child 'understands religion' (يعقل ديناً), meaning he can discern religious matters. Al-Hidayah adds another condition: if there is fear that the child may become accustomed to kufr (e.g., by participating in non-Muslim rituals), the child is taken away even before reaching that age. The commentary also addresses a grammatical point: the phrase 'أو يخاف' should have the jussive form (يخف) because it is conjoined to a jussive verb, but some scholars argue that 'أو' can mean 'until' or 'unless', affecting the parsing. The overall ruling is that a dhimmi mother's custody is conditional on the absence of religious harm to the child.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, gaining certain rights upon manumission or the master's death.
الذمية (al-dhimmiyyah): A non-Muslim woman living under the protection of an Islamic state, permitted to marry a Muslim man.
الخالة والدة (al-khalatu walidah): Hadith meaning 'the maternal aunt is like a mother', used as evidence for custody preference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which female relative has precedence over the sister from father in custody?
A) The paternal aunt
B) The maternal aunt
C) The maternal grandmother
D) The paternal grandmother

Key Takeaway
Free maternal relatives, especially the maternal aunt, are prioritized in Hanafi custody law, and freedom is a fundamental condition for all female custodians.

Custody of a Dhimmi Mother: Conditions and Limits
Commentary on the dhimmi mother's custody with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that can terminate a dhimmi mother's custody and apply the ruling to a scenario involving fear of religious harm.

Core Idea
A dhimmi mother retains custody of her child until the child understands religion or there is a risk of the child adopting kufr.

This passage clarifies that a non-Muslim mother (dhimmiyyah) has the same right to custody as a Muslim mother because affection is universal. However, her custody is limited by two conditions: the child reaching an age of religious understanding, or a reasonable fear that the child will become accustomed to kufr. The commentary also discusses a grammatical nuance in the Hidayah's phrasing.

Guided Path
1
Establish the general rule: dhimmi mother's equality
The text states that the dhimmi mother (e.g., Jewish or Christian) is like the Muslim mother in having custody of her child because affection does not differ by religion.
This applies when the father is Muslim and the mother is dhimmi; if both are dhimmis, the rule is different.
2
Identify the first condition: child understands religion
Custody continues 'until he understands religion' (حتى يعقل ديناً). Once the child can distinguish between faiths, the mother may lose custody to Muslim relatives.
The exact age is not specified; it depends on the child's capacity.
3
Identify the second condition: fear of kufr
Even before understanding religion, if there is fear that the child will become accustomed to kufr (e.g., participating in non-Muslim rituals), the child is taken away immediately.
This condition is added by al-Hidayah and must be observed even though not in the base text.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific case, determine whether the dhimmi mother retains custody or must surrender the child based on these two conditions.
If neither condition is met, she keeps custody. If either is met, custody is transferred to Muslim relatives.
5
Note the grammatical discussion (optional)
The commentator argues that 'yukhaf' should be jussive; others say 'aw' can mean 'until'. This does not change the ruling.
Focus on the substantive ruling.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the custody (hadanah) rights of female relatives. It begins by stating that paternal aunts (عمات) have custody rights in the same order as sisters but only if they are free. The condition of freedom is explained: an enslaved woman (أمة) and an umm walad (mother of a child from her master) have no right to custody because they are occupied with their master's service. However, if the child is also a slave, the mother is more entitled since the child belongs to the master. The commentary then discusses the dhimmi mother: she is like a Muslim mother in having custody of her child, as affection does not differ by religion. But the right is limited: until the child 'understands religion' (يعقل ديناً), meaning he can discern religious matters. Al-Hidayah adds another condition: if there is fear that the child may become accustomed to kufr (e.g., by participating in non-Muslim rituals), the child is taken away even before reaching that age. The commentary also addresses a grammatical point: the phrase 'أو يخاف' should have the jussive form (يخف) because it is conjoined to a jussive verb, but some scholars argue that 'أو' can mean 'until' or 'unless', affecting the parsing. The overall ruling is that a dhimmi mother's custody is conditional on the absence of religious harm to the child.

Key Terms
الذمية (al-dhimmiyyah): A non-Muslim woman living under the protection of an Islamic state, permitted to marry a Muslim man.
يعقل ديناً (ya'qilu dinan): The child reaches an age where he understands religious concepts and can distinguish between faiths.
يألف الكفر (ya'lafu al-kufr): The child becomes accustomed to disbelief through habits like attending non-Muslim worship or consuming forbidden items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi mother's custody is conditional on the child not understanding religion and no fear of kufr; both conditions must be absent for her to retain the right.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Two Conditions for Losing Custody: Understanding Religion and Fear of Kufr
Commentary adding a condition for loss of custody from Al-Hidayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which a Muslim child is removed from the custody of a non-Muslim mother according to the Hanafi school, and explain why the fear-of-kufr condition is necessary.

Core Idea
Custody ends when the child understands religion OR when there is fear of kufr habituation, even without understanding.

Custody (hadana) of a Muslim child with a non-Muslim mother is a delicate issue in Hanafi fiqh. The basic rule is that the mother retains custody as long as the child does not understand religion. However, Al-Hidayah introduces an additional protective condition: if there is a genuine fear that the child may become habituated to disbelief (kufr), the child must be removed even before reaching understanding. This lesson unpacks this ruling, its rationale, and the grammatical debate surrounding its formulation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions from Al-Hidayah
Read the passage from Al-Hidayah quoted in the commentary. It states: 'or the dhimmī woman has more right to her Muslim child as long as he does not understand the religions or it is feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief.' Identify the two conditions that terminate the mother's right.
The first condition is intellectual, the second is behavioral.
2
Understand the talil (reasoning) for the second condition
The commentator argues that the fear-of-kufr condition is necessary because 'habituation to disbelief may occur before understanding religion.' Think about children who imitate actions without comprehending their religious significance. Why would the law intervene before the child understands?
3
Examine the grammatical issue
The commentator points out that the verb 'yukhaf' (he fears) should be in the jussive case because it is conjoined to 'ya'qil' (he understands) after 'lam'. However, the text uses 'yukhāfu' (passive). The note suggests 'aw' here means 'until' or 'unless', making the jussive requirement unnecessary. Understand the two possible readings.
This grammatical discussion affects the precise legal meaning.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Imagine a young child who does not yet understand religion but accompanies his non-Muslim mother to her place of worship and participates in rituals. According to the passage, should he be taken from her custody? Use the two conditions to decide.
5
State the consequence of removal
The passage says 'he is removed from her' and 'placed with the Muslims'. What does this entail? The child is taken from the mother and given to a Muslim guardian or community. Why is this necessary?
The child's Islamic upbringing overrides maternal custody in this case.

[١] قوله : وفي «الهداية» عبارتها هكذا أو الذمية أحق بولدها المسلم ما لم يعقل الأديان أو يخاف أن يألف الكفر للنظر قبل ذلك، واحتمال الضرر بعده. [٢] قوله : يجب... الخ ؛ حاصله أن قوله : «يخاف»، معطوف على «يعقل»، وهو مجزوم بلم ، والمعطوف تابع للمعطوف عليه في الإعراب، فيجب أن يكون مجزوماً، فالصواب أن يقول : أو يخف. وجوابه: إنّه يمكن أن يكون أو بمعنى إلى أن» أو «إلا أن»، كما في قولهم : لألزمنك أو تعطيني حقي، كما ذكره في «النهاية» و«البناية»(۳) وغيرهما ، فالجزمُ بوجوب يخف بالجزم كما صدر عن الشارح ليس كما ينبغي، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالوجوب في كلامه الاستحسان. [٣] قوله : وهذا القيد ؛ يعني إن قيدَ عدمِ خوفِ ألفة الكفر المذكور في «الهداية»(4) لم يذكر في المتن ، ولا بُدَّ من ذكره، فقد لا يكون الصبي يعقل ديناً ، ولا يفهم محاسنَ الدين وقبائحه ، لكن يخاف تألفه الكفر، بأن يكون اعتاد مع الكفار الذهاب إلى معابدهم، والسجود لمعبوداتهم الباطلة، ونحو ذلك من الأفعال. [٤]قوله : ينزع ؛ أي يخرجُ من تحت يد الحاضنة ويضم إلى المسلمين، قال في «الفتح»: «وتمنع أن تغذيه الخمر ولحم الخنزير، وإن خيف ضُم إلى ناس من المسلمين (٥).
And in Al-Hidayah: 'As long as he [the child] does not understand religion, or it is feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief.' And his statement 'or it is feared' must be in the jussive case, which is 'yukhaf' because it is conjoined to a verb that is in the jussive due to 'lam'; thus the meaning is 'as long as he does not fear'. This condition was not mentioned in Al-Wiqayah, and it must be observed because habituation to disbelief may occur before understanding religion. So if it is feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief, he is removed from her. [Footnote 1] He said: In Al-Hidayah its wording is thus: 'Or the dhimmī woman has more right to her Muslim child as long as he does not understand the religions or it is feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief, for consideration before that and the possibility of harm after it.' [Footnote 2] He said: 'must...' etc.; its summary: His statement 'yukhaf' is conjoined to 'ya'qil' which is in the jussive due to 'lam', and the conjoined follows the conjoined in inflection, so it must be in the jussive, so the correct form is 'yukhaf'. The response: It is possible that 'aw' means 'until' or 'unless', as in their saying 'I will definitely stay with you until you give me my right' as mentioned in Al-Nihayah and Al-Binayah and others. Thus, the insistence on the necessity of 'yukhaf' being jussive as issued by the commentator is not as it should be, unless it is said that what is meant by 'wujub' in his speech is istihsan. [Footnote 3] He said: 'This condition' means that the condition of the absence of fear of habituation to disbelief mentioned in Al-Hidayah was not mentioned in the matn, and it must be mentioned. For the boy may not understand religion and not comprehend the beauties and evils of religion, but it is feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief, such as if he has become accustomed to going with the disbelievers to their places of worship, prostrating to their false objects of worship, and similar actions. [Footnote 4] He said: 'Yunza'' meaning he is taken out from under the care of the hadina and placed with the Muslims. He said in Al-Fath: 'And she is prevented from feeding him wine and pork, and if it is feared, he is placed with a group of Muslims.'
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from the commentator of Al-Wiqayah. The author notes that the condition 'or it is feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief' is found in Al-Hidayah but not in the base text (matn) of Al-Wiqayah. He argues this condition must be observed because a child may not yet understand religion but may still be at risk of becoming habituated to kufr through actions like visiting temples or bowing to idols. The commentary also addresses a grammatical point: the word 'yukhaf' should be in the jussive case like the verb it is conjoined to, but the author suggests it might be interpreted differently. The ruling is that custody continues until the child understands religion or until there is a fear of kufr habituation, in which case the child is taken from the hadina and placed with Muslims. The condition is based on the principle of protecting the child's faith.

Key Terms
تعقل الدين (ta'qqul al-din): The child's intellectual comprehension of religious concepts and the difference between belief and disbelief.
يألف الكفر (ya'lif al-kufr): The child becoming accustomed to or habituated to acts of disbelief, such as participating in non-Muslim rituals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following scenarios is the hadina's right to custody lost?
A) The child reaches puberty.
B) The child understands the religions.
C) The child is weaned.
D) The child memorizes the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi custody ends either when the child understands religion or when there is a genuine fear of kufr habituation, requiring removal to protect the child's faith.
