⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب النفقة
(والمطلقة الرجعي والبائن).
(1) وعمل القضاة اليومَ على هذا للحاجة. [1] قوله : على هذا ؛ أي على قول زفر له ، وإن كان خلاف مذهب مشايخنا الثلاثة للضرورة، وهذا من جملة المسائل العشرين التي أفتوا فيها للحاجة على قول زفر خلاف مذهب أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه . وقد نظمها العلامة محمد أمين المعروف بابن عابدين الشامي المتوفى سنة (١٢٥٠)(٢)، وذكر نظمه في حواشي المتعلقة بـ «الدر المختار» المسماة بـ «رد المحتار»(۳) فلتراجع. [۲] قوله : والمطلقة الرجعي والبائن ؛ في إطلاق البائن إشارة إلى عموم الحكم المعتدة البائن أعم من أن تكون مطلقة ثلاثاً أو ما دونه ، وفي إطلاق المطلقة إشارة إلى عموم الحكم للحامل وغير الحامل، ولو بدل المطلقة بالمعتدة لكان أولى ؛ لأن النفقة منوطة بالعدة ، ولا نفقة بعد العدة والوجه في ذلك أن النفقة بأنواعها الثلاثة إنما هي جزاء الاحتباس ، وهو كما يوجد في المنكوحة كذلك يوجد في معتدة الطلاق. ويشهد له قوله : ﴿وَإِن كُنَّ أُوْلَاتِ حَمْلٍ فَأَنفِقُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ حَتَّىٰ يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ﴾، وقوله : ﴿يَاأَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ إِذَا طَلَّقْتُمُ النِّسَاءَ فَطَلِّقُوهُنَّ لِعِدَّتِهِنَّ وَأَحْصُوا الْعِدَّةَ وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ رَبَّكُمْ لَا تُخْرِجُوهُنَّ مِن بُيُوتِهِنَّ﴾، وقوله : ﴿أَسْكِنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَنتُم﴾، فهذه الآيات بإطلاقها يشتمل على كل مطلقة.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Maintenance. (And the revocable and irrevocable divorcée). (1) And today the judges act upon this due to necessity. [1] His statement: 'upon this' means upon the statement of Zufar, even though it contradicts the madhhab of our three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) due to necessity. This is among the twenty issues in which they gave fatwa for necessity according to Zufar's statement, contrary to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and his two companions. The scholar Muhammad Amin known as Ibn 'Abidin al-Shami (d. 1250 AH) composed them in verse and mentioned them in his glosses on al-Durr al-Mukhtar called Radd al-Muhtar, so refer to it. [2] His statement: 'the revocable and irrevocable divorcée' – in the absolute expression of 'irrevocable' there is an indication of the generality of the ruling: the 'idda-observing divorcée, whether irrevocably divorced three times or less; and in the absolute expression of 'divorcée' there is an indication of the generality of the ruling for pregnant and non-pregnant. If instead of 'divorcée' it said 'woman observing 'idda' it would be more appropriate, because maintenance is contingent upon the 'idda, and there is no maintenance after the 'idda. The reasoning is that maintenance in its three types is compensation for being confined (ihtibas), and just as it is found in marriage, it is also found in the 'idda of divorce. This is supported by His statement: 'And if they are pregnant, then spend on them until they give birth' [65:6], and His statement: 'O Prophet, when you divorce women, divorce them for their 'idda and count the 'idda, and fear Allah your Lord. Do not expel them from their houses' [65:1], and His statement: 'Lodge them where you lodge' [65:6]. These verses in their absolute wording include every divorcée.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn ruling that maintenance is due to both revocable and irrevocably divorced women during their 'idda. The commentator explains that current judicial practice follows Zufar's opinion for necessity, even though the standard Hanafi position (of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) is different. This is one of the twenty well-known issues where later jurists issued fatwas based on Zufar's view due to practical need. The commentator then clarifies the scope: 'irrevocable divorcée' includes those divorced three times or less, and 'divorcée' includes pregnant and non-pregnant women. The underlying principle is that maintenance (food, clothing, lodging) is compensation for the woman's confinement (ihtibas) during 'idda, just as a wife is confined in marriage. The Quranic verses cited (65:1, 65:6) are adduced as proof for the generality of maintenance for all divorced women.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance covering food, clothing, and lodging due to the wife or divorcée during 'idda as compensation for her confinement.
الاحتباس (al-ihtibas): Legal confinement of the woman to the marital home during 'idda, for which maintenance is compensation.
زفر (Zufar): Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi jurist whose opinion is followed in these twenty issues for necessity.

A) Because she is still married to her husband.
B) Because she is confined (ihtibas) to the marital home.

D) Because she has no means of support.

Key Takeaway
Maintenance for all divorcées during 'idda is wajib in the Hanafi school, but judges follow Zufar's restrictive view for necessity.

Maintenance for Separation Without Sin and the Bain Divorcée Dispute
Ruling on maintenance for separation due to option, and Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on bain divorcée.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on maintenance for the bain divorcée and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the hadith of Fatima bint Qays.

Core Idea
A woman separated without sin gets maintenance; bain divorcée's right is disputed between Hanafi and Shafi'i.

In this lesson, we examine a key area of disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a woman who has been irrevocably divorced (bain) is entitled to maintenance and housing during her waiting period. The Hanafi school, relying on general Quranic verses and analogy, maintains she is. The Shafi'i school, citing the hadith of Fatima bint Qays, argues she is not. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh scriptural evidence and reconcile prophetic narration with broader principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that all 'idda-observing women except those separated due to their own sin are entitled to maintenance and housing. This includes the bain divorcée (non-pregnant) and women separated via khiyar al-`itq or lack of kafa'ah.
The basis is that separation without sin is analogous to divorce.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a non-pregnant irrevocably divorced woman (bain) does not receive maintenance or housing during 'idda.
The pregnant bain divorcée gets maintenance by consensus.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i uses the hadith of Fatima bint Qays, who reported that the Prophet did not give her maintenance or housing after her husband divorced her thrice.
This hadith is found in Muslim and the Sunan.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school treats this hadith as either abrogated by later Quranic commands (65:1, 65:6) or specific to Fatima due to her special circumstance (e.g., her outspoken nature). Thus, the general Quranic evidence takes precedence.
The Quran commands: 'Let them live where you live' and 'Provide for them.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Hanafis award maintenance and housing to bain divorcées; Shafi'is do not (unless pregnant). This affects financial support during the waiting period.
The difference is a direct consequence of divergent evidence weighting.

Source Text

والمفرقة بلا معصية كخيار العتق والبلوغ، والتفريق؛ لعدم الكفاءة النفقة والسكنى. [1] قوله : والمفرقة؛ اسم مفعول من التفريق؛ أي للمرأة التي فرقت من زوجها بلا معصية، والوجه في ذلك أن الفرقة بلا معصية في حكم الطلاق. [2] قوله : بلا معصية؛ أي من قبل الزوجة، فلو كانت الفرقة بمعصيتها فلها السكنى فقط، والحاصل: أن الفرقة إما من قبله أو من قبلها، فلو من قبله فلها النفقة مطلقاً، سواء كانت بمعصية أو لا، طلاقاً كان أو فسخاً، وإن كانت من قبلها، فإن كانت بمعصية فلا نفقة لها، ولها السكنى في جميع الصور. كذا في «البحر» [3] قوله : كخيار العتق؛ فإنه إذا طلبت الأمة التي أعتقت أو الصبية التي بلغت من زوجها الذي نكحها به مولاها أو وليها في حال رقها أو صغرها، وفسخت النكاح واعتدت فلها النفقة والسكني، وكذا إذا فسخ الأولياء نكاحها بعدم كفاءة الزوج، وقد مر تفصيل هذه المسائل في مواضعها. [4] قوله : النفقة والسكنى؛ المراد بالنفقة هاهنا الطعام بقرينة مقابلته بالسكني، ولم يذكر الكسوة؛ لأن العدة لا تطول غالباً فيستغنى عنها، فإن طالت المدة بأن كانت ممتدة الطهر مثلاً تجب الكسوة أيضاً. [5] قوله : وفي معتدة البائن؛ أي غير الحامل، فإن الحامل المبتوتة تستحق النفقة عنده أيضاً. [6] قوله : له حديث فاطمة رضي الله عنها؛ وهو حديث أخرجه مسلم وأصحاب السنن الأربعة وغيرهم مختصراً ومطوّلاً عنها أنها قالت: «طلقني زوجي ثلاثاً فلم يفرض لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سكنى ولا نفقة».
And the woman separated without sin, such as the option of emancipation, puberty, and annulment due to lack of equality (kafa'ah): maintenance and housing. [1] His statement: 'and the separated woman' – a passive participle from separation; meaning the woman who is separated from her husband without sin, and the reasoning is that separation without sin is in the ruling of divorce. [2] His statement: 'without sin' – meaning on the part of the wife. If the separation is due to her sin, then she gets housing only. The summary: separation is either from him or from her. If from him, she gets maintenance absolutely, whether with sin or not, whether divorce or annulment. If from her, then if without sin she gets both; if with sin, she gets housing in all cases. This is stated in al-Bahr. [3] His statement: 'such as the option of emancipation' – when the freed slave-woman or the minor who has attained puberty seeks annulment from her husband who married her while she was a slave or minor, and she annuls the marriage and observes 'idda, she gets maintenance and housing. Similarly if the guardians annul her marriage due to lack of kafa'ah of the husband. The details of these issues have been mentioned in their respective places. [4] His statement: 'maintenance and housing' – by maintenance here is meant food, by way of contrast with housing. Clothing is not mentioned because the 'idda usually is not long and is dispensed with. If the period is long, e.g., extended interval of purity, then clothing also becomes obligatory. [5] His statement: 'and for the bain (irrevocable) 'idda-observing woman' – meaning non-pregnant, for the pregnant irrevocably divorced woman gets maintenance according to him (Abu Hanifa) as well. [6] His statement: 'he (Shafi'i) has the hadith of Fatima (may Allah be pleased with her)' – this is a hadith reported by Muslim and the authors of the four Sunan, in abridged and full versions, that she said: 'My husband divorced me thrice, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not assign me housing or maintenance.'
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on maintenance for divorcées. It first addresses the case where separation occurs without fault on the wife's part, such as when a slave-woman exercises her option after emancipation (khiyar al-`itq), a minor exercises her option after attaining puberty (khiyar al-bulugh), or when the marriage is annulled due to the husband's lack of kafa'ah (equality). In such cases, the woman is entitled to both maintenance (food) and housing during her 'idda. The commentator explains that separation without sin is treated like divorce in this regard. If the separation is due to the wife's sin (e.g., apostasy or disobedience), she gets only housing, not food. The commentator then clarifies that 'maintenance' here specifically refers to food, as housing is separately mentioned. Clothing is omitted because 'idda is typically short, but if it extends (e.g., due to a long period between periods), clothing becomes obligatory. The passage then turns to the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the bain (irrevocable) divorcée. Abu Hanifa holds that even a non-pregnant irrevocably divorced woman gets maintenance and housing during 'idda. The pregnant one gets it by consensus. Shafi'i argues using the hadith of Fatima bint Qays, who reported that the Prophet did not give her maintenance or housing after her husband divorced her thrice. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is abrogated or specific, and the general Quranic verses take precedence. The hadith is presented as proof for Shafi'i.

Key Terms
المفرقة بلا معصية (al-mufarraqah bi-la ma'siyah): A woman separated from her husband through annulment without any fault on her part, such as khiyar al-`itq or khiyar al-bulugh.
خيار العتق (khiyar al-`itq): The option of emancipation: a female slave who is married while a slave may annul the marriage upon gaining freedom.
الكفاءة (al-kafa'ah): Equality in social status and lineage between spouses, a condition for valid marriage in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does a woman separated due to her own sin receive during 'idda?
A) Maintenance and housing.
B) Housing only.
C) Maintenance only.
D) Neither maintenance nor housing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school entitles all 'idda-observing women except those separated by sin to maintenance and housing; the bain divorcée dispute illustrates competing claims of Quranic generality and Hadith specificity.

Nafaqah and Suknah in Ba'in 'Iddah: Hanafi Position vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi commentary with Shafi'i dispute on nafaqah/suknah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah and suknah for a woman in ba'in iddah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the hadith of Fatima bint Qais.

Core Idea
For ba'in iddah, lodging is wajib but maintenance is not — the husband's right of return triggers nafaqah.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the rulings for a woman separated from her husband without sin, clarifying when she is entitled to maintenance (nafaqah) and lodging (suknah). The focus then shifts to the specific case of ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, where the Hanafi school holds that only lodging is due, while the Shafi'i school argues for both. The dispute centers on the interpretation of the hadith of Fatima bint Qais and the Quranic verse 'Do not expel them from their houses.' This lesson unpacks the arguments and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify types of separation
Distinguish separation from the husband's side vs. wife's side, and with/without sin. If from husband: both nafaqah and suknah. If from wife with sin: only suknah. If from wife without sin: both.
The commentator summarizes: 'If from him, she has maintenance absolutely... from her, with sin, no maintenance, lodging in all cases.'
2
Locate the specific case of ba'in divorce
The passage then addresses 'mu'taddah al-ba'in' (non-pregnant). The Shafi'i school claims she deserves both nafaqah and suknah.
The Shafi'i rely on the first hadith of Fatima bint Qais and general qiyas on iddah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi response cites a second narration from Fatima where the Prophet explicitly ties nafaqah to the right of return (raj'ah), and highlights the rejection of the first hadith by Umar and Aisha.
The Quranic verse 65:1 (do not expel them) is used to prove suknah.
4
Examine the weakness of the opposing hadith
The commentator notes the second narration is weak in chain, but the Hanafi position is strengthened by the Quranic verse and the Companion rejection.
Al-Zayla'i detailed the weakness in Nasb al-Rayah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position: for non-pregnant ba'in iddah, lodging is wajib, nafaqah is not. For pregnant ba'in, nafaqah is due as per another rule.
Imam Muhammad held that even lodging is not wajib, but the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمفرقة بلا معصية كخيار العتق والبلوغ، والتفريق لعدم الكفاءة النفقة والسكنى. قوله: والمفرقة بلا معصية: أي للمرأة التي فرقت من زوجها بلا معصية، والوجه في ذلك أن الفرقة بلا معصية في حكم الطلاق. قوله: بلا معصية: أي من قبل الزوجة، فلو كانت الفرقة بمعصيتها فلها السكني فقط. والحاصل: أن الفرقة إما من قبله أو من قبلها، فلو من قبله فلها النفقة مطلقاً، سواء كانت بمعصية أو لا، طلاقاً كان أو فسخاً. وإن كانت من قبلها، فإن كانت بمعصية فلا نفقة لها، ولها السكنى في جميع الصور. قوله: كخيار العتق: فإنه إذا طلبت الأمة التي أعتقت أو الصبية التي بلغت من زوجها الذي نكحها به مولاها أو وليها في حال رقها أو صغرها، وفسخت النكاح واعتدت فلها النفقة والسكني. وكذا إذا فسخ الأولياء نكاحها بعدم كفاءة الزوج. قوله: النفقة والسكنى: المراد بالنفقة هاهنا الطعام بقرينة مقابلته بالسكني، ولم يذكر الكسوة؛ لأن العدة لا تطول غالباً فيستغنى عنها، فإن طالت المدة بأن كانت ممتدة الطهر مثلاً تجب الكسوة أيضاً. قوله: وفي معتدة البائن: أي غير الحامل، فإن الحامل المبتوتة تستحق النفقة عنده أيضاً. له حديث فاطمة رضي الله عنها. ولنا: رد عمر. وفي رواية عنها عند النسائي وأحمد والطبراني: إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لها: «اسمعي يا بنت قيس، إنما النفقة للمرأة على زوجها ما كانت عليها رجعة، فإذا لم يكن عليها رجعة فلا نفقة لها ولا سكنى». وهذه الرواية ضعيفة، لا يحتج بسندها كما بسطه الزيلعي في «نصب الراية». قوله: ولنا رد عمر: يعني قد رد عمر بن الخطاب حديث فاطمة رضي الله عنها حيث قال لما سمع روايتها: لا نترك كتاب ربنا ولا سنة نبينا بقول امرأة لا ندري حفظت أم نسيت. لها السكنى والنفقة، قال الله: لَا تُخْرِجُوهُنَّ مِنْ بُيُوتِهِنَّ وقد ثبت الرد على حديث فاطمة رضي الله عنها أيضاً عند عائشة عن البخاري وغيره، وكذا عن غيرهما من الصحابة، فإذن لم يبق ذلك الحديث الذي رد عليه جمع من الصحابة له محتجاً به.
And the separated woman without sin, like the option of emancipation and puberty, and separation due to lack of equivalence, (has) maintenance and lodging. His statement: 'and the separated woman without sin' means the woman who has been separated from her husband without sin, and the reason for that is that separation without sin is in the ruling of divorce. His statement: 'without sin' means from the wife's side. If the separation was due to her sin, she has lodging only. The summary: separation is either from him or from her. If from him, she has maintenance absolutely, whether with sin or not, whether divorce or annulment. If from her, then if with sin, no maintenance for her, and she has lodging in all cases. His statement: 'like the option of emancipation' – if the freed slave woman or the girl who has reached puberty requests from her husband whom her master or guardian married her to while she was a slave or minor, and she annuls the marriage and observes 'iddah, she has maintenance and lodging. Likewise, if the guardians annul her marriage due to lack of equivalence of the husband. His statement: 'maintenance and lodging' – what is meant by maintenance here is food, by way of contrasting it with lodging, and clothing is not mentioned because the 'iddah usually does not last long and is dispensed with. If the period becomes long, such as if she has an extended period of purity, clothing is also obligatory. His statement: 'and regarding the separated woman of irrevocable divorce' – meaning non-pregnant, for a pregnant irrevocably divorced woman deserves maintenance in his view as well. He has the hadith of Fatima (may Allah be pleased with her). And we have the rejection of 'Umar. And in a narration from her with al-Nasa'i, Ahmad, and al-Tabarani: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to her: 'Listen, O daughter of Qais: maintenance is for the woman from her husband as long as he has the right of return. When he has no right of return, there is no maintenance for her and no lodging.' This narration is weak; its chain is not used as evidence, as al-Zayla'i explained in Nasb al-Rayah. His statement: 'and we have the rejection of 'Umar' – meaning 'Umar ibn al-Khattab rejected the hadith of Fatima (may Allah be pleased with her) when he heard her narration: 'We do not leave the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the statement of a woman – we do not know whether she remembered or forgot. She has lodging and maintenance. Allah said: 'Do not expel them from their houses.' And the rejection of the hadith of Fatima (may Allah be pleased with her) has also been confirmed from 'A'isha via al-Bukhari and others, and likewise from other Companions. Therefore, that hadith which a group of Companions rejected is no longer a valid argument.
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is a commentator’s expansion on a ruling from al-Wiqayah regarding the right to maintenance (nafaqah) and lodging (suknah) during the waiting period (ʿiddah) for a woman who is separated from her husband without any sin on her part. The commentator first clarifies the general rule: if the separation originates from the husband, the woman receives both nafaqah and suknah regardless of whether it is a divorce or annulment. If the separation originates from the wife, she only receives suknah if the separation is due to her sin; if without sin, she gets both nafaqah and suknah. The examples given are the wife’s option of emancipation (khiyar al-ʿitq) or puberty (khiyar al-bulugh), and annulment due to lack of equivalence (kafa’ah). The commentator then focuses on the specific case of a woman in ba’in (irrevocable) divorce who is not pregnant. According to the Shafiʿi school, such a woman is entitled to both nafaqah and suknah, citing the hadith of Fatima bint Qais that the Prophet ﷺ did not give her nafaqah or suknah, implying that if she were entitled they would have been given. The Hanafi response is twofold. First, they present the rejection of this hadith by ʿUmar ibn al-Khattab, who prioritized the Quranic verse (65:1) “Do not expel them from their houses” which implies the right to lodging and, by extension, maintenance. Second, they bring a different narration of Fatima bint Qais herself (reported by al-Nasa’i, Ahmad, and al-Tabarani) where the Prophet ﷺ explicitly states that nafaqah is only for a woman whose husband has the right of return (rajʿah); thus a ba’in woman gets neither. The commentator notes this second narration is considered weak by some, but the overall Hanafi position is strengthened by the rejection of the first hadith by multiple Companions, including ʿA’isha. Therefore, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that a woman in ba’in ʿiddah does not receive nafaqah, but lodging is still obligatory based on the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance during iddah, typically food and clothing, owed to the wife under certain conditions.
سكنى (suknah): Lodging or housing provided during the iddah period.
معتدة البائن (muʿtaddah al-baʾin): A woman observing iddah after an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) where the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage.
رجعة (rajʿah): The right of the husband to take back his wife during the iddah of a revocable divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nafaqah is wajib (obligatory).
B) Nafaqah is not wajib, but suknah is.
C) Both nafaqah and suknah are wajib.
D) Neither nafaqah nor suknah is wajib.

Key Takeaway
For non-pregnant ba'in iddah, the Hanafi school holds that lodging (suknah) is obligatory but maintenance (nafaqah) is not, based on the Quranic command and Companion rejection of the opposing hadith.

Hanafi Refutation of Fatimah bint Qays Hadith on Nafaqah
Hanafi argument using Sahaba rejection to counter a hadith on nafaqah/sukna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on housing and maintenance for a ba'in divorcee, explain the Hanafi refutation of the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays using the rejection of 'Umar, and compare it with the opposing view.

Core Idea
The Hanafis reject the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays as weak, relying on 'Umar's objection and Qur'an 65:1 to grant housing to ba'in divorcees.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute on whether an irrevocably divorced woman (ba'in) is entitled to housing (sukna) and maintenance (nafaqah) during her 'iddah. The Hanafi school defends her right to housing based on the Qur'an and the rejection of a contrary hadith by the Companions. Understanding this argument reveals how the Hanafis prioritize certain sources over others.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate what the Hanafi school rules for a ba'in divorcee regarding housing and maintenance.
Housing is wajib; maintenance is not wajib unless pregnant.
2
Identify the opposing view and their proof
Describe the view that denies both housing and maintenance, and identify the hadith they rely on.
Opponents use the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Trace how 'Umar's rejection and the Qur'anic verse support the Hanafi position.
The verse 'Do not expel them from their houses' is key.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith
Explain why the Hanafis consider the hadith weak and how they respond to it.
Weak chain and Sahaba rejection.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in rulings between the two positions.
Hanafi: housing granted; opposing: no housing.

Book of Divorce/Chapter of Maintenance
Fatimah bint Qays
(1)
And our proof: the rejection of 'Umar
(1)-
And in a narration from her [Fatimah] according to al-Nasa'i, Ahmad, and al-Tabarani: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to her: 'Listen, O daughter of Qays: maintenance is only for the woman from her husband as long as she has a right of return (raj'ah); so if she has no right of return, then there is no maintenance for her and no housing.' This narration is weak; its chain is not used as evidence, as al-Zayla'i explained in 'Nasb al-Rayah' (3).
[1] His saying: 'And our proof: the rejection of 'Umar' means that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab rejected the hadith of Fatimah (may Allah be pleased with her) when he heard her narration. He said: 'We do not leave the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the statement of a woman; we do not know whether she memorized or forgot. She is entitled to housing and maintenance. Allah said: Do not expel them from their houses (65:1).' (1) (0) Muslim narrated it.
(4)
And the rejection of the hadith of Fatimah (may Allah be pleased with both) has also been established with 'A'ishah from al-Bukhari and others, and likewise from other Companions. So that hadith, which a group of Companions rejected, is no longer a proof.
(1) It is from Abu Salamah from Fatimah bint Qays that her husband divorced her during the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and was spending on her maintenance. When she saw that, she said: 'By Allah, I will certainly inform the Messenger of Allah. If I am entitled to maintenance, I will take what is sufficient for me; if I am not entitled to maintenance, I will not take anything from him.' She said: 'So I mentioned that to the Messenger of Allah, and he said: 'You have no maintenance and no housing.'' In Sahih Muslim (2:1114), wording is his, and in al-Sunan al-Kubra li al-Nasa'i (5:394), and others. (2) It is from Abu Ishaq: I was with al-Aswad ibn Yazid sitting in the Great Mosque, and with us was al-Sha'bi. Al-Sha'bi narrated the hadith of Fatimah that the Messenger of Allah did not give her housing or maintenance. So al-Aswad took a handful of pebbles and threw them at him, then said: 'Woe to you! You narrate such a thing? 'Umar said: 'We do not leave the Book of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, and the Sunnah of His Prophet for the statement of a woman; we do not know whether she memorized or forgot. She is entitled to housing and maintenance. Allah said: Do not expel them from their houses.' [al-Talaq: 1] (2) In Sahih Muslim (2:1118), and Musnad Abi 'Awanah (3:183), and Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kubra (7:475), and others.
(3) Nasb al-Rayah (5:365)
(4) al-Talaq: from verse 1.
(5) In Sahih Muslim (2:1118), and others.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays concerning maintenance (nafaqah) and housing (sukna) for an irrevocably divorced woman (ba'in). The author, 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, is a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, a Hanafi fiqh text. The passage begins by stating that the Hanafi proof is the rejection of the hadith by 'Umar ibn al-Khattab. It then quotes a version of the hadith from al-Nasa'i and others indicating that maintenance is only due as long as there is a right of return (raj'ah), and if there is no return, no maintenance or housing is due. The Hanafis consider this version weak, as al-Zayla'i explained in Nasb al-Rayah.

In the commentary, the author explains that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab rejected the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays when he heard it, saying that the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Prophet cannot be abandoned for the statement of a single woman whose memory is uncertain. 'Umar then cited the Qur'anic verse (65:1) which commands not to expel women from their houses, implying that housing is due. The rejection of this hadith is also reported from 'A'ishah and other Companions. Therefore, the hadith that was rejected by a group of Companions is not a valid proof. Thus, the Hanafi position is that a ba'in woman is entitled to housing (based on the verse) but not to maintenance (unless pregnant), while those who accept the hadith (such as al-Shafi'i) argue for no housing or maintenance altogether.

The passage then provides two variant narrations in the footnotes to document the hadith and the objection. In summary, the Hanafis argue that the hadith of Fatimah bint Qays is weak and cannot override the explicit Qur'anic text, so the ruling follows the general implication of the verse for housing, and maintenance is limited to the case of pregnancy or raj'i divorce.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance: financial support including food, clothing, and shelter that a husband is obligated to provide to his wife during marriage and to his divorced wife during her 'iddah under certain conditions.
سكنى (sukna): Housing: the right to reside in the marital home during the 'iddah period.
رجعة (raj'ah): The right of the husband to take back his wife during the 'iddah without a new marriage contract after a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i).
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman who is observing the waiting period ('iddah) after divorce or death of her husband.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants housing to ba'in divorcees based on the Qur'an and the Companions' rejection of the hadith, upholding a stronger textual authority.

Nafaqah During 'Iddah: Exclusions for Death and Sin
Detailed rulings on who is not entitled to nafaqah during 'iddah: women in 'iddah of death and those separated due to sin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on nafaqah for women in 'iddah of death and those separated due to sin, and distinguish between ba'in and raj'i cases regarding apostasy and enabling.

Core Idea
Nafaqah ceases when 'iddah is for the woman's own right (death) or her sin causes the separation.

In this lesson, we examine who is not entitled to nafaqah during 'iddah. The Hanafi school makes a crucial distinction between 'iddah for the husband's right and 'iddah for the woman's own right, as well as between sins that affect the separation and those that do not. Understanding these exceptions is essential for correctly applying maintenance rules in family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two excluded categories
Locate in the passage: the woman in 'iddah of death (mu'taddah al-mawt) and the woman separated due to sin (al-mufarraqah bi al-ma'siyah).
The text opens with 'لا لمعتدة الموت، والمفرقة بالمعصية'.
2
Understand the reasoning for each exclusion
For death, her 'iddah is for the right of the Shari'ah, not the husband. For sin, she becomes like a nashizah because she detains herself without right.
The commentary emphasizes: 'لأن احتباسها ليس لحق الزوج، بل لحق الشرع' and 'لأنها صارت حابسة نفسها بغير حق'.
3
Analyze the examples of sin
Two examples are given: apostasy (riddah) and kissing the husband's son (taqbil ibn al-zawj). Note that apostasy drops maintenance for a ba'in woman, but enabling does not.
The text says: 'ردة معتدة الثلاث تسقط، لا تمكينها ابنه'.
4
Differentiate between ba'in and raj'i
For a ba'in woman (irrevocably divorced), apostasy drops nafaqah (she is imprisoned), but enabling does not. For a raj'i woman (revocably divorced), both apostasy and enabling drop nafaqah because they cause the final separation.
The key is: 'لأن الفرقة لم تقع بالطلاق، بل بمعصيتها' for raj'i.
5
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a woman's status (ba'in or raj'i) and her act (apostasy or enabling), determine whether nafaqah continues or ceases.
Use the table from the lesson to guide your answer.

Not for the woman observing 'iddah from death, nor the one separated due to sin: such as apostasy, and kissing the husband's son. Apostasy of a woman in 'iddah of three divorces drops [maintenance], but not her enabling her son[-in-law] to kiss her; because apostasy and enabling have no effect on the separation, since it was already established before them, so they do not drop maintenance. However, the apostate woman is imprisoned to repent, and there is no maintenance for the imprisoned one, unlike the one who enables the husband's son.
[1] His saying: 'Not for the woman observing 'iddah from death' means maintenance and housing are not obligatory for a woman who observes 'iddah due to the death of her husband, because her confinement is not for the right of the husband, but for the right of the law; therefore, menstruation is not considered in her 'iddah in order to know the purity of the womb, so maintenance is not obligatory upon the husband. As in al-Hidayah.
[2] His saying: 'And the one separated' is conjoined to 'woman of death'; i.e., no maintenance for the one who is separated due to sin on her part, because she becomes one who detains herself without right, like a nashizah (disobedient wife).
[3] His saying: 'Kissing the husband's son' can be genitive to the object or to the subject; i.e., her kissing the husband's son or the husband's son kissing her.
[4] His saying: 'Woman of three divorces' – mentioning 'three' is incidental, following al-Hidayah; otherwise the ruling includes all ba'in women.
The conclusion: If a woman irrevocably divorced (mabtutah) apostatizes during the 'iddah, her maintenance drops, but not if she enables her husband's son and he kisses her with desire. In contrast, for a woman with a revocable divorce (raj'i), if she cooperates with her husband's son or he kisses her with desire, her maintenance drops, because the separation did not occur by divorce but by her sin. As in al-Bahr.
[5] His saying: 'Drops' is imperfect from isqat, and its pronoun refers to the subject, which is apostasy.
[6] His saying: 'Not her enabling' – genitive to the subject and its object 'her son'; i.e., the enabling of the irrevocably divorced woman of her husband's son does not drop maintenance, and he [the author] restricts 'enabling' to avoid coercion.
[7] His saying: 'Except that...' – its summary: The apostate woman drops her maintenance only because she is imprisoned for repentance, and the imprisoned one has no maintenance, unlike the one who enables. In short, apostasy and enabling have no effect on the separation, because it occurred before them by the irrevocable divorce.
(8) His saying: 'The one who enables' is agent noun from tamkin; i.e., the woman who enables her husband's son and he kisses her, then she does not leave his house, so maintenance does not drop.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from a Hanafi commentary. It explains who is not entitled to nafaqah (maintenance) during the 'iddah period. The author first lists those for whom nafaqah is not due: (1) a woman observing 'iddah from the death of her husband (mu'taddah al-mawt), and (2) a woman separated due to sin (al-mufarraqah bi al-ma'siyah), such as apostasy and kissing the husband's son.

In the commentary, each part is unpacked. For the woman in 'iddah of death, maintenance is not due because her confinement ('iddah) is not for the right of the husband but for the right of the Shari'ah. The purpose is to observe a period of mourning and to ensure no pregnancy from the deceased husband, which is a personal right of the widow. Since the husband has no claim on her, maintenance is not obligatory. This is from al-Hidayah.

For the woman separated due to sin, she is considered like a nashizah (disobedient wife) because she detains herself without right. The two examples given are apostasy (riddah) and kissing the husband's son (taqbil ibn al-zawj). The author then differentiates between a woman divorced irrevocably (ba'in, e.g., three divorces) and one divorced revocably (raj'i). For a ba'in woman, apostasy during 'iddah drops her maintenance, but enabling her husband's son to kiss her does not drop maintenance. For a raj'i woman, both apostasy and enabling drop maintenance because the separation is caused by her sin, not the original divorce.

The reasoning is that apostasy and enabling do not affect the separation itself because the separation (the divorce) already occurred before these acts. For a ba'in woman, the divorce is complete, so apostasy does not change the fact that she is already separate; but she is imprisoned for apostasy, and the imprisoned have no maintenance. Enabling, however, does not lead to imprisonment, so maintenance remains. For a raj'i woman, the divorce is revocable, so her sin of apostasy or enabling actually causes the final separation, thus dropping maintenance.

The author concludes that the apostate woman's maintenance drops because she is imprisoned, while the one who enables is not, so her maintenance does not drop.

Key Terms
معتدة الموت (mu'taddah al-mawt): A woman who is observing the 'iddah after the death of her husband. The 'iddah is four months and ten days (or until delivery if pregnant).
مفرقة بالمعصية (mufarraqah bi al-ma'siyah): A woman whose separation from her husband is caused by her own sin, such as apostasy or engaging in forbidden acts (e.g., kissing the husband's son with desire).
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam. In the context of marriage, apostasy by either spouse causes immediate separation (faskh).
تمكين (tamkin): Enabling: allowing the husband's son to kiss her with desire without coercion.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocably divorced; refers to a woman divorced three times or divorced for a consideration (khul'), where the husband cannot revoke the divorce during 'iddah without a new contract.
رجعي (raj'i): Revocably divorced; refers to a woman divorced once or twice where the husband may take her back during the 'iddah without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because her 'iddah is for the right of Allah, not for the right of the husband.
C) Because the husband's estate is not responsible for her upkeep.
D) Because she is considered independent after the death.

Key Takeaway
Nafaqah is not due for 'iddah of death or when separation is caused by the woman's sin, with further distinctions between ba'in and raj'i regarding apostasy and enabling.

Nafaqah During ʿIddah: The Effect of Apostasy and Misbehavior
Commentary distinguishing nafaqah for different divorcees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings on nafaqah for different types of divorcees during ʿiddah and state whether apostasy or enabling a kiss cancels nafaqah.

Core Idea
Apostasy cancels nafaqah for the finally divorced woman; a kiss from the husband's son does not.

This lesson examines a passage from the Hanafi commentary tradition that clarifies the impact of a wife's actions during ʿiddah on her right to maintenance. We will see how the type of divorce (revocable vs. final) and the nature of the action (apostasy vs. enabling a kiss) determine the ruling, following the distinctions made by the authors of al-Hidayah and al-Bahr. By the end, you will be able to apply these distinctions to new scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of women discussed
The passage covers three types: (1) woman in ʿiddah of death, (2) woman who caused separation through sin (e.g., apostasy), (3) finally divorced woman (bāʾin) who apostatizes or enables a kiss. Notice the base text and commentary structure.
2
Extract the ruling for each category
For ʿiddah of death: no nafaqah. For the one who caused separation through sin: no nafaqah. For the finally divorced: apostasy cancels nafaqah, but enabling a kiss does not. The revocably divorced woman is contrasted: her nafaqah is cancelled by a kiss.
The term 'triple divorce' is incidental; the ruling covers all final divorces.
3
Understand the reasoning behind each ruling
For ʿiddah of death: confinement is for a religious right, not the husband's right. Apostasy cancels nafaqah because the apostate is imprisoned for repentance, and the imprisoned has no nafaqah. Enabling a kiss does not affect the separation since the divorce is already final.
For revocable divorce, the kiss is a sin that causes separation, so nafaqah falls.
4
Apply the distinction between final and revocable divorce
The key difference: for a final divorcee, the separation is already complete, so later sins (except apostasy that leads to imprisonment) do not affect nafaqah. For a revocable divorcee, the marriage is still intact until ʿiddah ends, so her sin can terminate the right.

Not for the woman in iddah of death, and the one who caused separation through sin: such as apostasy, and the kiss from the husband's son, and the apostasy of a woman in iddah of triple divorce cancels (nafaqah), but not her enabling of his son (to kiss her); because apostasy and enabling have no effect on the separation; since it had been established before them, so they do not cancel nafaqah, except that the apostate woman is imprisoned for repentance, and there is no nafaqah for the imprisoned, unlike the one who enabled her husband's son. [1] His statement: 'Not for the woman in iddah of death' means that nafaqah and housing are not obligatory for a woman who observes iddah due to her husband's death; because her confinement is not for the right of the husband, but for the right of the law; therefore menstruation was not considered in her iddah to know the purity of the womb, so nafaqah is not obligatory on the husband. Thus in al-Hidayah. [2] His statement: 'and the one who caused separation' is coordinated with 'woman in iddah of death'; meaning no nafaqah for the one who caused separation through sin on her part; because she has imprisoned herself without right, so she becomes like a disobedient wife (nashizah). [3] His statement: 'and the kiss from the husband's son' can be with the addition to the object or to the subject; i.e., her kissing the husband's son or the husband's son kissing her. [4] His statement: 'woman in iddah of triple divorce' – the mention of triple is incidental, following al-Hidayah; otherwise the ruling includes all types of final (ba'in) divorce. The summary: If the finally divorced woman apostatizes during the iddah, her nafaqah is cancelled, but not if she enables her husband's son and he kisses her with desire; unlike the revocably divorced woman if she willingly submits to her husband's son or he kisses her with desire, for her nafaqah is cancelled because the separation was not by divorce but by her sin. Thus in al-Bahr. [0] His statement: 'cancels' is a present tense verb from cancellation, and its pronoun refers to the subject, which is apostasy. [6] His statement: 'not her enabling' is with the addition of the subject and its object 'his son'; i.e., nafaqah is not cancelled by the enabling of the finally divorced woman of her husband's son (to kiss her), and he excludes coercion by using 'enabling'. [7] His statement: 'except that...' its summary: The apostate woman's nafaqah is cancelled only because she is imprisoned for repentance, and the imprisoned has no nafaqah, unlike the one who enables; and in summary, neither apostasy nor enabling has any effect on the separation because it occurred before them through the final divorce. (8) His statement: 'the one who enabled' is a participle from enabling; i.e., the one who enabled her husband's son and he kissed her, for she does not leave his house, so nafaqah is not cancelled by it.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a legal ruling concerning nafaqah (maintenance) for women undergoing ʿiddah (waiting period) after divorce or death, specifically addressing the effect of apostasy (riddah) and misbehavior (like a kiss from the husband's son). The base ruling states that nafaqah is not obligatory for a woman in iddah of death, nor for one who caused separation through sin (e.g., apostasy). However, the commentary clarifies that apostasy by a finally divorced (bāʾin) woman cancels her nafaqah, but permitting her husband's son to kiss her does not cancel it, because the separation was already complete before those actions. In contrast, for a revocably divorced (rajʿī) woman, submitting to a kiss from the husband's son cancels nafaqah because the separation is not yet final and her sin effects it. The reasoning is that apostasy leads to imprisonment for repentance, and an imprisoned woman has no nafaqah, while the one who enables a kiss does not leave her husband's house. The author follows al-Hidayah and al-Bahr. The passage also notes that the term 'triple divorce' is incidental; the ruling applies to all final divorces. The commentary explains each phrase of the base text in detail, emphasizing the distinction between the two scenarios.

Key Terms
الردة (al-riddah): Apostasy from Islam; in this context, it is a sin that causes separation and cancels nafaqah for a finally divorced woman in ʿiddah.
التمكين (al-tamkīn): Enabling or permitting; specifically here, the wife enabling her husband's son to kiss her with desire. This does not cancel nafaqah for a finally divorced woman.
المعتدة (al-muʿtaddah): A woman observing the waiting period (ʿiddah) after divorce or death of her husband. The ruling on nafaqah varies based on the type of separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the nafaqah of a finally divorced woman if she commits apostasy during her ʿiddah?
A) Her nafaqah is cancelled because she is imprisoned for repentance.
B) Her nafaqah is not cancelled because apostasy does not affect the separation.
C) Her nafaqah is cancelled only if she also enables a kiss.
D) Her nafaqah is increased as a punishment.

Key Takeaway
Apostasy cancels nafaqah for a finally divorced woman because she is imprisoned; enabling a kiss does not cancel it since the separation is already final.

Mother's Nursing Obligation and Father's Duty to Hire
States ruling that mother is not required to nurse unless designated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mother's nursing obligation, explain the condition of ta'ayyun, and distinguish between qada'an and diyanatan obligations.

Core Idea
Mother is not compelled to nurse; father must provide, except when she is the only option.

The issue of nursing a child after divorce often leads to conflict between parents. The Hanafi school provides a clear framework: the mother is not legally forced to nurse, but the father is financially responsible. This passage from *'Umdat al-Ri'ayah* explains the general rule, the exception when the mother must nurse, and the father's duty to hire a wet nurse—with important restrictions on hiring the mother herself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Locate the initial statement: the mother is not obligated to nurse judicially (qada'an). Understand that this means a court cannot compel her.
The phrase 'qada'an' is key; it refers to enforceable legal obligation.
2
Understand the exception (ta'ayyun)
Find the condition 'unless she is designated' – when no other wet nurse exists or the child refuses other milk. In that case, she must nurse both legally and religiously.
Ta'ayyun transforms a non-obligatory act into a wajib.
3
Recognize the father's duty to hire
The father must hire a wet nurse if the mother is not designated. The commentary stresses that this is part of maintenance, which is solely his responsibility.
The father cannot shift this cost to the mother or relatives.
4
Analyze restrictions on hiring the mother
Hiring the mother is invalid if she is still married or in revocable iddah (raj'i). For irrevocable divorce (ba'in), there are two narrations.
The restriction prevents conflict with marital rights and custody.
5
Distinguish qada'an vs diyanatan
The commentary clarifies that the mother is religiously (diyanatan) encouraged to nurse, but not legally bound unless designated.
Diyanatan obligations are moral, not enforceable by a judge.

Source Text

And his mother is not obligated to nurse him unless she is designated, and the father hires someone to nurse him at her house, and if he hires her while she is married, or in the waiting period of a revocable divorce, to nurse him, it is not permissible; and in the case of an irrevocable divorce, two narrations. Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the obligation of nursing and who bears the cost. The core ruling states that the mother is not judicially obligated to nurse her child unless she is the only available option. The father must hire a wet nurse, and the nursing should take place at the mother's home to respect her custody rights. However, if the father hires the mother herself while she is still married or in a revocable iddah (raj'i), it is not permissible. For the case of an irrevocably divorced (ba'in) mother, there is a difference of narration (riwayatan), which will be discussed in the next lesson. The commentary explains that the obligation to nurse falls under maintenance (nafaqah), which is solely the father's responsibility. The mother is religiously (diyanatan) encouraged to nurse, but not compelled by the court unless she is the only possible nurse for the child's well-being. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on the father's financial liability and the mother's right to compensation for nursing if she is not the only option.

Key Terms
إرضاع (irdāʿ): The act of breastfeeding a child, which, in this context, is a service that the father must provide for by hiring a nurse.
قضاءً وديانة (qaḍā'an wa diyānatan): Two aspects: qaḍā'an refers to the enforceable legal obligation in court; diyānatan refers to the religious or moral duty before Allah, not enforceable by a judge.
المبتوتة (al-mabtūtah): A woman who has been irrevocably divorced (ba'in), such that the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage contract.

The mother is not compelled to nurse; the father must provide, but if she is the only option, nursing becomes obligatory on her both legally and religiously.

Two Narrations on Hiring the Irrevocably Divorced Mother as Nurse
Records two contradictory Hanafi narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi narrations on hiring a ba'in mother as a nurse and identify which position is mufta bihi according to later authorities.

Core Idea
Marriage ends but some effects remain—hence two valid narrations on hiring the ba'in mother.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of a father hiring his irrevocably divorced (ba'in) wife to nurse their child during her iddah period. The passage presents two contradictory riwayat (narrations) and notes the preferences of later scholars. Understanding this dispute is essential for appreciating how the Hanafi school accommodates multiple authentic transmissions and how later jurists determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
Locate the two positions in the text: one permits hiring, the other prohibits it. Note that each is traced to a different transmission chain.
The first narration is attributed to some as 'zahir al-riwayah'; the second is narrated by al-Hasan from Imam Abu Hanifa.
2
Examine the proofs for each
The permissibility narration analogizes the ba'in mother to a stranger after iddah. The prohibition narration cites remaining marital effects, such as iddah itself.
Each proof relies on a different aspect of the legal relationship after irrevocable divorce.
3
Note the preferences of later sources
The text mentions that al-Jawharah prefers the permissibility view, while al-Tatarkhaniyyah and al-Fath favor impermissibility. Understand how these sources are weighed.
Later fatwa sources often settle disputes based on practical considerations and strength of transmission.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
According to al-Tatarkhaniyyah, the fatwa is upon impermissibility. However, the author notes that some consider the permissibility narration as 'zahir al-riwayah'. Identify which is operative today.
The mufta bihi is generally the latter view (impermissibility) per later authorities, but the dispute remains acknowledged.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a father hires the ba'in mother, is the contract valid? Under the first view, yes; under the second, no, and he must hire another.
This difference directly impacts family law practice and the validity of the nursing contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روایتان
[1] قوله : روايتان ; في رواية : تجوز استئجارها ؛ لأنّ النكاح قد زال، كما يجوز استئجار أم الصبي ا المطلقة بعد انقضاء العدة. وفي رواية : لا ؛ لأنّ النكاح باق في حق بعض الأحكام، وذكر في «الجوهرة» (۳) : أن القول الأول أصح، وذكر في «التاتارخانية»: أنّ الفتوى على الثاني ورجحه في «الفتح» أيضاً. (۱) وهما : الأولى : الجواز : قال بعضهم هي ظاهر الرواية، وصححها صاحب «الجوهرة» (۲ : ۸۹). والثانية : عدمه وبه رواية الحسن عن الإمام، ويؤمئ إليها كلام (الهداية ٢ : ٤٦)، ويدل عليها ظاهر كلام القُدُوري (ص (۸۲) ، وفي النهر»: وهي الأولى، وفي التاتارخانية»: وعليه الفتوى.
Two narrations. [1] His statement: two narrations; in one narration: hiring her is permissible because the marriage has ended, just as it is permissible to hire the mother of the child who is divorced after the waiting period expires. And in another narration: no, because the marriage remains in effect with respect to some rulings. And it is mentioned in al-Jawharah that the first view is more correct, and mentioned in al-Tatarkhaniyyah that the fatwa is upon the second, and it was preferred in al-Fath as well. (1) And they are: the first is permissibility; some said it is the apparent narration, and it was corrected by the author of al-Jawharah (2:89). The second is impermissibility, and with it is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam, and it is indicated by the words of al-Hidayah (2:46), and it is indicated by the apparent words of al-Quduri (p. 82), and in al-Nahr: it is the first, and in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: and upon it is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute: Is it permissible for a father to hire his irrevocably divorced (ba'in) wife to nurse their child during her iddah? The text records two transmissions. The first, which some consider the 'zahir al-riwayah' (apparent transmission), permits it by analogizing to a mother after iddah. The second, transmitted by al-Hasan from Imam Abu Hanifa, prohibits it because certain effects of marriage remain during iddah (e.g., iddah itself). The author notes that later authorities differed on which is preferred: al-Jawharah prefers the permissibility view, while al-Tatarkhaniyyah and al-Fath side with impermissibility. This difference impacts practice: a father following the first view may hire the mother; following the second, he must hire a different woman. The student should note that here, weight is given to both positions, and the fatwa is ultimately on the second (impermissibility) according to some later sources, but the first is defended as sound.

Key Terms
رواية (riwāyah): A transmission or narration reporting a legal opinion from an early imam, especially from Abu Hanifa or his students.
الظاهر الرواية (al-ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or well-known transmission from the founding imams, typically from the six books of Imam Muhammad.
مبتوتة (mabtūtah): A woman who has been irrevocably divorced (ba'in) such that the marriage cannot be renewed except by a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains two valid narrations on hiring the ba'in mother; the mufta bihi is impermissibility, but the permissibility view is also well-attested.

The Principle of No Obligation Beyond Capacity (La Taklif Illa bi al-Wus')
Extracts the principle of no obligation beyond capacity from Quran 2:233.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle of no obligation beyond capacity, identify its proof from Quran 2:233, and apply it to a fiqh scenario.

Core Idea
Islamic law never obligates what is beyond human capacity – this is a foundational Hanafi maxim.

This lesson focuses on one of two major legal principles derived from the Quranic verse on nursing and maintenance (2:233). The principle 'la taklif illa bi al-wus' (no obligation beyond capacity) is a cornerstone of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Understanding this maxim helps us see how classical scholars derived broad legal rules from specific Quranic texts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the proof text
Read the beginning of Quran 2:233 as quoted in the source: 'No soul is burdened except within its capacity.' This phrase is the direct dalil for the principle.
The full verse covers nursing, but the principle is general.
2
Analyze the wording
The phrase 'لا تكلف نفس إلا وسعها' is a negative statement implying negation of obligation beyond capacity. In Hanafi usul, such a form indicates a general prohibition of burdening beyond capacity.
Word 'وسع' means ability.
3
Understand the principle's scope
The author states: 'this is a comprehensive principle from which many particular branches derive.' This means the principle applies to all Sharia obligations, not just nursing.
Examples: concessions in prayer, fasting, etc.
4
Apply to a subsidiary case
Consider a person who cannot stand due to illness. Under this principle, they are not obliged to pray standing; they may pray sitting.
This is one of the many furu' that flow from this maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَن يُتِمَّ الرَّضَاعَةَ وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ لَا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسُ إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَا تُضَارَ وَلِدَةٌ بِوَلَدِهَا وَلَا مَوْلُودٌ لَهُ بِوَلَدِهِ، وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ فَإِنْ أَرَادَا فِصَالًا عَن تَرَاضٍ مِّنْهُمَا وَتَشَاوُرٍ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا وَإِنْ أَرَدتُّمْ أَن تَسْتَرْضِعُوا أَوْلَدَكُمْ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا سَلَّمْتُم مَّا وَالَيْتُمُ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ ) . (٤) دلّ على جملة من المسائل والفوائد على ما بسطه المفسرون في كتبهم : ١ . منها : أن لا تكليف شرعاً بما ليس في الوسع ، يؤخذ ذلك من قوله : لَا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسُ إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا * - بضم الواو وسكون السين – بمعنى القدرة والطاقة، وهذا أصل كلي تتفرع منه فروع جزئية كثيرة. ٢ . ومنها : إنّ النسب إلى الآباء دون الأمهات ؛ يؤخذ ذلك من قوله : وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ
Know that the saying of Allah Most High: 'And mothers shall nurse their children for two complete years for whoever wishes to complete the nursing period. And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable. No soul is burdened except within its capacity. No mother shall be harmed on account of her child, nor father on account of his child. And upon the heir is similar. And if they both desire weaning by mutual consent and consultation, there is no sin upon them. And if you desire to seek nursing for your children, there is no sin upon you when you hand over what you have given according to what is acceptable. And fear Allah and know that Allah is All-Seer of what you do.' (4) indicates a number of issues and benefits as expounded by the commentators in their books: 1. Among them: that there is no legal obligation to do what is beyond one's capacity, taken from His statement: 'No soul is burdened except within its capacity' – with dammah on the waw and sukun on the sin – meaning ability and capacity, and this is a comprehensive principle from which many particular branches derive. 2. And among them: that lineage is traced to fathers, not mothers; taken from His statement: 'And upon the father' (wa 'ala al-mawludi lahu).
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the well-known 'verse of nursing' (ayat al-rida') from Surah al-Baqarah. The author highlights two major legal principles derived from this verse. First, the principle of 'no obligation beyond capacity' (la taklif illa bi al-wus') is extracted from the phrase 'لا تكلف نفس إلا وسعها'. This is a foundational maxim in Islamic jurisprudence, meaning that Islamic law never commands something impossible or unbearably difficult. It underlies many subsidiary rulings, such as concessions in prayer, fasting, and other acts. Second, the verse indicates that lineage (nasab) is attributed to the father, not the mother. The proof is that the duty of maintenance is placed on 'al-mawludu lahu' (the one to whom the child is born), i.e., the father. This is a key point in family law: children are ascribed to their fathers' lineage, even though the mother gives birth. The passage thus demonstrates how one Quranic verse can yield multiple legal principles through careful tafsir and usul al-fiqh methodology.

Key Terms
وسع (wusʿ): Capacity or ability; the limit of what a person can bear without undue hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which part of Quran 2:233 is cited as proof for the principle of no obligation beyond capacity?
A) 'وعلى المولود له رزقهن'
B) 'لا تكلف نفس إلا وسعها'
C) 'فإن أرادا فصالاً عن تراض'
D) 'وعلى الوارث مثل ذلك'

Key Takeaway
The Quranic negation of burden beyond capacity establishes a universal Hanafi maxim that no Sharia obligation is valid if it exceeds the individual's ability.

The Principle of Patrilineal Descent (Nasab ila al-Ab)
Derives the principle that lineage is traced to fathers from the phrase 'وعلى المولود له' in Quran 2:233.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proof from Quran 2:233 that lineage is traced to fathers, and explain its legal implications in Hanafi family law.

Core Idea
Lineage in Islam is traced through the father, not the mother, based on Quranic attribution of maintenance responsibility.

This lesson examines the second legal principle derived from the verse on nursing (2:233): that a child's lineage (nasab) is attributed to the father, not the mother. This principle has far-reaching effects on inheritance, marriage prohibitions, and guardianship. The proof is subtle but powerful: the verse places the duty of maintenance on 'al-mawludu lahu' – the one to whom the child is born – which implies paternal connection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key phrase
The author cites 'وعلى المولود له' (and upon the father) as the proof. The term 'المولود له' literally means 'the one for whom the child is born' – that is, the father.
The Arabic word 'المولود' (child) plus the preposition 'له' (for him) indicates possession or connection.
2
Understand the legal inference
The verse imposes financial responsibility on the father. This responsibility is linked to his relationship with the child, which is defined by lineage (nasab). Thus, the duty to provide proves that the child is ascribed to him.
Hanafi usul uses this 'dalalat al-iltizam' (necessary implication).
3
Contrast with the mother's role
The mother is mentioned as the nurse (الوالدات), but the father is specified as the one liable for expenses. This asymmetry indicates that lineage is through the paternal line, not maternal.
The verse does not say 'upon the mother' for responsibility.
4
Apply the principle
In Hanafi law, a child born in a valid marriage is automatically attributed to the husband. This rule governs inheritance (child inherits from father), guardianship (father is natural guardian), and marriage prohibitions (siblings are defined by father's side).
Exception: li'an (mutual imprecation) can negate paternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَن يُتِمَّ الرَّضَاعَةَ وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ لَا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسُ إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَا تُضَارَ وَلِدَةٌ بِوَلَدِهَا وَلَا مَوْلُودٌ لَهُ بِوَلَدِهِ، وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ فَإِنْ أَرَادَا فِصَالًا عَن تَرَاضٍ مِّنْهُمَا وَتَشَاوُرٍ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا وَإِنْ أَرَدتُّمْ أَن تَسْتَرْضِعُوا أَوْلَدَكُمْ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا سَلَّمْتُم مَّا وَالَيْتُمُ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ ) . Seven Rulings Derived from the Breastfeeding Verse
Commentary extracting seven rulings from the verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven rulings derived from Āyat al-Raḍā' (2:233) and explain the linguistic or contextual basis for each.

Core Idea
One verse yields seven distinct rulings through careful linguistic analysis and legal deduction.

This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of istinbāṭ (derivation) from the Qur'an. The commentator takes a single verse about breastfeeding and extracts seven separate legal rulings, each grounded in a specific phrase or construction. Understanding this process is key to grasping how Hanafi fiqh builds rules from scripture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary verse
Recognize that all derivations come from al-Baqarah 2:233, which is quoted in full. Read the verse carefully.
2
Locate each ruling and its proof phrase
For each of the seven rulings, find the specific part of the verse used as evidence (e.g., 'lā tukallifu' for the first ruling, 'wa ʿalā al-mawlūdi lahu' for the second, etc.)
3
Understand the linguistic mechanism
Note how the commentator uses grammar to derive rulings: khabar in meaning of amr, lām of specification, etc.
This is the core of Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh.
4
Classify the nature of the obligation
Distinguish between obligations that are dīyānan (religious) vs. qaḍā'an (legal). The sixth ruling states breastfeeding is wajib dīyānan.
5
Apply the rulings to practical scenarios
Consider how each ruling would apply in a real case, such as what happens if a mother refuses to breastfeed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق نفقة الأقارب
روایتان
اعلم أن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ ﴾ أوجب الإرضاع على الأمهات
[١] قوله : روايتان ؛ في رواية : تجوز استئجارها ; لأنّ النكاح قد زال، كما يجوز استئجار أم الصبي المطلقة بعد انقضاء العدة.
وفي رواية : لا ; لأنّ النكاح باق في حق بعض الأحكام، وذكر في «الجوهرة» : أن القول الأول أصح، وذكر في «التاتارخانية»: أنّ الفتوى على الثاني ورجحه في «الفتح» أيضاً. (۱)
[٢] قوله : أوجب ; اعلم أن قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم في سورة البقرة : ﴿ وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَن يُتِمَّ الرَّضَاعَةَ وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ رِزْقُهُنَّ وَكِسْوَتُهُنَّ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ لَا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسٌ إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا لَا تُضَارَّ وَالِدَةٌ بِوَلَدِهَا وَلَا مَوْلُودٌ لَهُ بِوَلَدِهِ وَعَلَى الْوَارِثِ مِثْلُ ذَلِكَ فَإِنْ أَرَادَا فِصَالًا عَن تَرَاضٍ مِّنْهُمَا وَتَشَاوُرٍ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا وَإِنْ أَرَدتُّمْ أَن تَسْتَرْضِعُوا أَوْلَادَكُمْ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا سَلَّمْتُم مَّا آتَيْتُم بِالْمَعْرُوفِ وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ ﴾
دلّ على جملة من المسائل والفوائد على ما بسطه المفسرون في كتبهم :
١. منها : أن لا تكليف شرعاً بما ليس في الوسع ، يؤخذ ذلك من قوله : ﴿ لَا تُكَلِّفُ نَفْسٌ إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا ﴾ - بضم الواو وسكون السين – بمعنى القدرة والطاقة، وهذا أصل كلي تتفرع منه فروع جزئية كثيرة.
٢. ومنها : إنّ النسب إلى الآباء دون الأمهات ; يؤخذ ذلك من قوله : ﴿ وَعَلَى الْمَوْلُودِ لَهُ ﴾ بلام الاختصاص ; أي على الذي ولد الولد لأجله، ومختصاً به منسوباً إليه، وهذا هو النكتة في اختيار هذه العبارة على ما هو أخصر منه، مثل: وعلى والده وغير ذلك، وقد بسط الأصوليون هذا البحث في بحث إشارة النص.
٣. ومنها : إنّ مدة الرضاعة حولان ، ولا تجوز بعد الحولين ، يدل عليه قوله تعالى : ﴿ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ ﴾ ، ويشهد له قوله في سورة الأحقاف: ﴿ وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلَاثُونَ شَهْرًا ﴾ إشارة إلى أقل مدة الحمل، وهو ستة أشهر، وأكثر مدة الرضاعة، وهو حولان، وقد مر ما يتعلّق بهذا المقام في موضعه فتذكره.
٤. ومنها : إنّه يجوزُ الفطام قبل تمام حولين بعد تراضي الوالدين، وبتشاور من أهل البصيرة يدلّ عليه قوله : ﴿ فَإِنْ أَرَادَا فِصَالًا ﴾ : أي قبل تمام الحولين، وإنما اعتبر تراضيهما مع التشاور اهتماماً بالولد ; لئلا يفطم في وقت يضره الفطام، ولا يريد أحد الوالدين ضررا به.
٥. ومنها: إنّه تجوز إجارة المراضع للرضاعة، يدل عليه قوله : ﴿ وَإِنْ أَرَدتُّمْ أَن تَسْتَرْضِعُوا ﴾ الخ; فإن معناه : وإن أردتم أيها الآباء أن تسترضعوا أولادكم مراضع غير أمهاتهم إن أبت أمهاتهم أن يرضعن لعذر فلا أثم عليكم في ذلك إذا فرضتم إلى المراضع ما أردتم إيتاء من أجرة الرضاع ونحوها والتسليم شرط ندب لا شرط جواز إجماعاً.
٦. ومنها : إنّ الرضاعة واجبة على الوالدة إلا لعذر وعجز، يدل عليه قوله : ﴿ وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ ﴾ ، فإنّه خبر في معنى الأمر، والمعنى: والوالدات يجب عليهن أن يرضعن أولادهن ، وهذا الوجوبُ إنّما هو ديانة، حتى لو لم ترضع الولد بلا عذر شرعي أثمت لا قضاء، فإنّها إن امتنعت لا يجبر القاضي كما مر ذكره.
٧. ومنها : حرمة مضارّة الوالدين ، يدل عليه قوله : ﴿ لَا تُضَارَّ ﴾ ، وهو يحتمل أن يكون صيغة معروف ، فأصلها : تضارر - بكسر الراء الأولى – ، ويحتمل أن يكون صيغة مجهول.
(۱) وهما : الأولى : الجواز : قال بعضهم هي ظاهر الرواية، وصححها صاحب «الجوهرة» (۲ : ۸۹). والثانية : عدمه وبه رواية الحسن عن الإمام، ويؤمئ إليها كلام «الهداية» (٢ : ٤٦)، ويدل عليها ظاهر كلام القُدُوري (ص ۸۲) ، وفي «النهر»: وهي الأولى، وفي «التاتارخانية»: وعليه الفتوى.
Book of Divorce: Maintenance of Relatives. Two narrations. Know that Allah's saying: 'And the mothers shall breastfeed their children...' made breastfeeding obligatory upon mothers. [1] His statement: 'Two narrations': In one narration: It is permissible to hire her because the marriage has ended, just as it is permissible to hire the divorced mother of the child after the waiting period ends. In another narration: No, because the marriage remains in effect regarding some rulings. And it is mentioned in 'al-Jawhara' that the first opinion is more correct, and it is mentioned in 'al-Tatarkhaniyya' that the fatwa is on the second, and he preferred it in 'al-Fath' as well. (Footnote: They are: first: permissibility, some said it is the apparent narration, and the author of al-Jawhara corrected it (2:89). Second: impermissibility, and by it is the narration of Hasan from the Imam, and the words of al-Hidayah (2:46) indicate it, and the apparent words of al-Quduri (p. 82) support it, and in al-Nahr: it is the first, and in al-Tatarkhaniyya: and upon it is the fatwa.) [2] His statement: 'made obligatory'. Know that His statement in Surah al-Baqarah: 'And the mothers shall breastfeed their children for two complete years for those who wish to complete the breastfeeding, and upon the father is their provision and clothing in the known manner. No soul shall be burdened except with its capacity. A mother shall not be harmed because of her child, nor a father because of his child. And upon the heir is similarly. Then if both desire weaning by mutual consent and consultation, there is no sin upon them. And if you wish to seek wet nurses for your children, there is no sin upon you when you hand over what you agreed in the known manner. And fear Allah and know that Allah sees what you do.' This indicates a number of issues and benefits as the commentators have elaborated in their books: 1. Among them: There is no legal obligation beyond capacity, taken from His statement: 'No soul shall be burdened except with its capacity' – with dammah on the waw and sukun on the sin – meaning ability and capacity. This is a universal principle from which many particular branches derive. 2. Among them: Lineage is to fathers, not mothers, taken from His statement: 'And upon the one to whom the child is born' with the lam of specification, meaning upon the one for whom the child was born, specified and attributed to him. This is the subtlety in choosing this phrase over a more concise one like 'and upon his father' etc. The scholars of principles have elaborated on this in the discussion of indication of the text. 3. Among them: The duration of breastfeeding is two years, and it is not permissible after two years, indicated by His statement: 'for two complete years', and supported by His statement in Surah al-Ahqaf: 'And his carrying and his weaning is thirty months' indicating the minimum duration of pregnancy, which is six months, and the maximum duration of breastfeeding, which is two years. And what relates to this topic has passed in its place, so recall it. 4. Among them: It is permissible to wean before completing two years after mutual consent of the parents and consultation of people of insight, indicated by His statement: 'Then if both desire weaning' – i.e., before completing the two years. Their mutual consent along with consultation is considered out of care for the child, lest he be weaned at a time that harms him, and neither parent intends harm to him. 5. Among them: It is permissible to hire wet nurses for breastfeeding, indicated by His statement: 'And if you wish to seek wet nurses...' For its meaning is: If you fathers wish to seek wet nurses other than the mothers for your children if the mothers refuse to breastfeed due to an excuse, there is no sin on you in that if you hand over to the wet nurses what you intend to give from the breastfeeding fee and the like, and handing over is a condition of recommendation, not a condition of validity, by consensus. 6. Among them: Breastfeeding is obligatory upon the mother unless there is an excuse or incapacity, indicated by His statement: 'And the mothers shall breastfeed their children,' for it is a khabar in the meaning of a command. The meaning is: The mothers must breastfeed their children. This obligation is only a religious obligation, such that if she does not breastfeed the child without a valid excuse, she sins but there is no legal enforcement, for if she refuses, the judge does not compel her, as has been mentioned. 7. Among them: The prohibition of parents harming each other, indicated by His statement: 'Do not harm,' which can be a verb in the active voice, its original form is 'tadārara' – with kasrah on the first ra – or it can be a verb in the passive voice.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āya, a supercommentary on Sharḥ al-Wiqāya, deals with the legal rulings (aḥkām) derived from the Quranic verse on breastfeeding (Āyat al-Raḍā', al-Baqarah 2:233) and a related intra-madhhab dispute on hiring a divorced mother as a wet nurse. The commentator first clarifies the context: the chapter is on divorce and maintenance of relatives (nafaqat al-aqārib). He then introduces a dispute (riwāyatān) regarding the permissibility of hiring the divorced mother to breastfeed her child after the marriage has ended. One narration allows it, arguing that the marriage bond has terminated, so no impediment remains. The second prohibits it, reasoning that some effects of the marriage persist. The commentator notes that al-Jawhara al-Nayyira declared the first narration more correct, but al-Tatarkhāniyya and al-Fatḥ al-Qadīr state that the fatwa is on the second (prohibition). The footnote adds that the first is considered Ẓāhir al-Riwāya by some, while the second is the narration of Ḥasan ibn Ziyād from the Imam, and that the latter is the operative position. The commentator then proceeds to extract seven legal benefits from the verse. First, the principle that no one is obligated beyond their capacity ('adam al-taklīf bi-mā laysa fī al-wus'), derived from 'lā tukallifu nafsun illā wus'ahā'. Second, that lineage is attributed to fathers, not mothers, inferred from the phrase 'wa ʿalā al-mawlūdi lahu' using the lām of specification. Third, that the maximum breastfeeding period is two complete years (ḥawlān kāmilān), and breastfeeding after that is not valid, supported by the verse in Sūrat al-Aḥqāf. Fourth, that weaning before two years is permissible with mutual parental consent and consultation. Fifth, that hiring wet nurses is permissible, derived from 'wa in aradtum an tastarḍiʿū'. Sixth, that breastfeeding is obligatory (wājib) on the mother, unless excused, but this obligation is dīyānatan (religious/moral) not qaḍā'an (legally enforceable), so the judge does not compel her. Seventh, the prohibition of parents harming each other (ḥurmat muḍārrat al-wālidayn), derived from 'lā tuḍārra'. The passage demonstrates the method of istinbāṭ (derivation) from the Qur'an, using linguistic indications and contextual reasoning.

Key Terms
روایتان (riwāyatān): Two narrations (transmissions) within the Ḥanafī school regarding a particular ruling
ديانة (diyānatan): Religious/moral obligation, as opposed to legal enforceability (qaḍā'an). The mother is sinful if she refuses, but the state does not compel her.
إجارة المراضع (ijārat al-marāḍiʿ): Hiring wet nurses (women to breastfeed children)
خبر بمعنى الأمر (khabar bi-ma'nā al-amr): A declarative sentence that carries the meaning of a command, used to derive obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the nature of the obligation of breastfeeding on the mother?
A) It is a legal obligation enforceable by the judge.
B) It is a religious obligation (diyānatan), not legally enforceable.
C) It is prohibited to refuse breastfeeding under any circumstance.
D) The mother may be compelled by the judge to breastfeed.

Key Takeaway
The verse yields seven rulings, including the obligation of breastfeeding as a religious duty, not enforceable by the state.
