The Book of Manumission: Ambiguous Manumission. So by the first pronouncement half of the dower of one woman falls away, halved between the excluded (wife) and the confirmed (wife): so one-quarter of the dower of each fell. Then by the second pronouncement the quarter fell, halved between the confirmed and the incoming (wife): so each got one-eighth, so three-eighths of the confirmed's dower fell by the two pronouncements, and one-eighth of the incoming's dower fell. And this issue was posed only for divorce before consummation, so that the first pronouncement causes irrevocable separation, so what the first pronouncement affected no longer remains a locus for the second pronouncement, so it becomes in this meaning like manumission. The confirmed (wife) divorced her, and the excluded becomes specified in the first pronouncement, and the first pronouncement is not invalidated because at the moment it was issued both were certainly wives. Unlike the first case where the second pronouncement is invalidated by specifying the confirmed in the first. If the husband did not clarify his intent from the two pronouncements and one of the three women died, then death is a clarification. If the excluded died, the confirmed becomes specified for the first pronouncement and the second pronouncement is invalidated for the reason mentioned. If the confirmed died, the excluded becomes specified for the first pronouncement and the incoming for the second. If the husband dies without clarification, it is said their death distributes the ruling of divorce upon them, and the dowers drop according to the detail mentioned, because the divorce was before consummation, and it drops half the dower. This is in the commentaries of the Book of Ziyadat. [1] His statement: 'halved' — that is because if he knew the intended meaning that one of them was the confirmed or the excluded, that woman would be specified as the one receiving the divorce, and half her dower would fall. Since he did not know, that falling half is shared equally between them, so from each of them one-quarter of her dower fell. [2] His statement: 'the quarter fell' — because divorce before consummation drops half the dower, but it is contingent on the absence of doubt about its validity, and it was mentioned earlier that the second pronouncement is dubious between its validity and invalidity, so it drops half of half, which is the quarter. [3] His statement: 'causes irrevocable separation' — meaning irrevocable separation from the one divorced by it, because divorce before consummation does not require waiting period, but she becomes irrevocable as if divorced, and another divorce does not fall upon her after that due to lack of marital locus. [4] His statement: 'like manumission' — so just as in the manumission issue mentioned earlier, the one manumitting by the first pronouncement... Some scholars said: This is a statement particular to Muhammad, and it is said it is the statement of both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to this narration, they must differentiate between manumission and divorce, which is that the first pronouncement in both manumission and divorce necessitates halving between the excluded and the confirmed. When (the wife) died without clarification, it became clear that in the case of manumission, as it was discussed, it became halved between them. It did not remain a locus for the second pronouncement, and therefore what the second affected was deposited, and it spread in its two halves, and what the first affected fell as detailed previously, so too here. [1] His statement: 'this' — meaning what was mentioned in the text about the fall of one-quarter of the incoming's dower, one-eighth of the excluded's dower, and three-eighths of the confirmed's dower. [2] His statement: 'particular' — but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), one-quarter of the incoming's dower falls as in the manumission case, and their statement and his statement in manumission were elaborated earlier. [3] His statement: 'they must differentiate' — meaning since the divorce case is agreed upon, they must show the difference between the manumission case and the divorce case, where he said in the manumission case: half of both the external and internal (slaves) are freed, and in the divorce case: one-quarter of the excluded's dower and one-eighth of the incoming's dower fall, and the analogy of their statement in manumission would be that they say here that one-quarter of the incoming's dower also falls. As for according to Muhammad's statement, there is no need to show a difference, because he ruled in both cases in the same pattern, as he ruled in the chapter of manumission that one-quarter of whoever entered the second pronouncement is freed, and ruled here that one-eighth of the dower of the one who entered the second pronouncement falls. [4] His statement: 'that the first pronouncement...' etc.; summary: The difference is that the confirmed (slave) in the manumission case is fit to receive the second pronouncement, so he enters the second pronouncement, and the manumission established by it is distributed to the internal and the confirmed; so half of the internal is freed due to the absence of an obstacle, and from the confirmed one-quarter, because the half that affected him with the second is common in his two halves, and half of him was freed by the first pronouncement, so by this pronouncement one-quarter is freed. Unlike the confirmed (wife) in the divorce case, for she is dubious between being fit for the second pronouncement and not being fit for it. [0] His statement: 'necessitates' — because his statement addressing his two slaves: 'One of you is free,' and likewise his statement to his two wives: 'One of you is divorced,' necessitates halving between them. So if the intended meaning from the ambiguous (pronouncement) becomes clear, then that is it, and if he does not clarify...
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya' is a commentary on a base text dealing with ambiguous divorce (al-talaq al-mubham) within the chapter of manumission. The ruling concerns a scenario where a man has three wives and makes two ambiguous divorce pronouncements before consummation: first 'one of you is divorced' (addressed to two wives, the 'excluded' and the 'confirmed'), then 'one of you is divorced' (addressed to the remaining two, the 'confirmed' and the 'incoming'). Since divorce before consummation is irrevocable (ba'in), the first pronouncement severs the marital tie with one of the two addressed wives, making the second pronouncement applicable only to the other. The author explains the distribution of half dower: by the first pronouncement, half the dower of one wife falls, but since it is ambiguous which one, that half is shared equally between the two addressed, so each loses a quarter. Then by the second pronouncement, a quarter falls (half of the remaining half), but since it is ambiguous between the confirmed and incoming, that quarter is shared, so each loses an eighth. Thus the confirmed loses a total of 3/8 (quarter + eighth), the excluded loses nothing, and the incoming loses 1/8. The text then discusses the effect of death of one wife before clarification: death serves as a clarification, specifying which pronouncement applies to whom. The key intra-Hanafi dispute is between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani? Actually 'qawlahu' refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, i.e., the Sahibayn). Imam Muhammad holds that the ruling is analogous to the manumission case previously discussed, where the second pronouncement affects only the incoming, resulting in one-eighth of her dower falling. The Sahibayn disagree, arguing that in divorce the confirmed wife is not fully eligible for the second pronouncement, so the distribution differs. The commentary elaborates the distinction: in manumission, the confirmed slave remains eligible for all pronouncements, but in divorce, the confirmed wife becomes completely ineligible for a second divorce due to irrevocability. Therefore, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) rule that one-quarter of the incoming's dower falls, consistent with the manumission analogy, while Imam Muhammad rules that only one-eighth falls. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but later Hanafi works tend to follow Imam Muhammad's view in ambiguous divorce as the authoritative one.

Key Terms
مبهم (mubham): Ambiguous or unspecified; in this context, a divorce pronouncement that does not specify which wife is intended.
إيجاب (ījāb): Pronouncement or statement effecting a legal consequence, here the utterance of divorce or manumission.
بينونة (baynūna): Irrevocable separation; divorce before consummation is ba'in sughra, not revocable.
تنصيف (tansīf): Dividing equally between two parties; here, the ambiguous effect is split between the two possible wives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous triple divorce before consummation, the mahr is distributed by halving the ambiguous effects, but the intra-Hanafi dispute over the incoming wife's loss (1/8 vs 1/4) turns on whether the confirmed wife remains eligible for a second pronouncement.

Talaq — Divorce

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Second Ambiguous Pronouncement in Manumission and Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on second pronouncement effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the effect of a second ambiguous pronouncement in manumission and divorce, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf in terms of share distribution.

Core Idea
The second pronouncement's effect depends on whether the fixed party is a fitting subject, leading to different shares across manumission and divorce.

This passage unfolds a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement about ambiguous pronouncements (ījāb maʿ al-ibhām) when the speaker dies before specifying his intent. The core question: does the second pronouncement affect the 'fixed' party (the one already partially determined by the first pronouncement) identically in manumission and divorce? Muhammad holds a uniform rule; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's other narration require differentiation. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how legal presumptions about subjecthood affect share distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A master says to two slaves 'one of you is free' (ambiguous), then later (or after his death) either makes a second similar pronouncement or dies before specifying. The same scenario with a husband saying to two wives 'one of you is divorced'. Determine what legal effects are at stake.
The first pronouncement creates apportionment (tansif) or ambiguity (taraddud) depending on the imam's view.
2
State the positions of the three imams
Abu Hanifa: first pronouncement immediately frees half of each slave, making each partially free. Abu Yusuf: first pronouncement creates a state of ambiguity (taraddud) like a mukatab. Muhammad: uniform ruling in manumission and divorce – the second pronouncement frees one-quarter of the entering slave or drops one-eighth of the entering wife's dower.
The text focuses on Muhammad's view and the alternative view where Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differentiate.
3
Analyze the reasoning for differentiation
The key is whether the 'fixed' party (the wife or slave already affected by the first pronouncement) is a suitable subject for the second pronouncement. In manumission, the fixed slave is partially free and thus can be a subject; in divorce, the fixed wife's status is more ambiguous and she cannot fully be a subject.
The second pronouncement must be performative (not a report) and requires a valid subject.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Muhammad's uniform view, the shares are the same in both manumission and divorce (1/4 entering, 1/8 exiting? Actually the text says 1/4 of entering slave freed, 1/8 of entering wife's dower falls – not identical fractions but analogous reasoning). Under the differentiating view, the shares differ: in manumission, the fixed slave also receives a share (1/4 from second pronouncement); in divorce, the fixed wife's share is reduced because she is not a full subject.
The precise shares: entering wife loses 1/8 dower, exiting wife loses 1/4, fixed wife loses 3/8. This is the ruling in the text.
5
Connect to the principle of performative utterance
The principle is that a performative act (ījāb) takes effect immediately unless a preventing impediment (māniʿ) such as ambiguity (ibhām) exists. Here, the ambiguity prevents immediate full effect, causing apportionment or ambiguity. Upon death without clarification, the law retroactively determines the effect as if it operated from the start.
This ties to Hanafi usul: al-amm yufidu al-wujub? Actually it's about performatives.

[1] قوله : هذا ؛ أي ما ذكر في المتن من سقوط ربع مهـر الداخلة، وثمن مهر الخارجة، وثلاثة أثمان الثابتة.

[٣] قوله : لا بد لهما من الفرق ؛ يعني لما كانت مسألة الطلاق اتفاقية فلا بد أن يبين الفرق بين صورة العتق وصورة الطلاق، حيث قال في صورة العتق : تعتق نصف الخارج والداخل كليهما، وفي صورة الطلاق بسقوط ربع مهر الخارجة، وثمن مهر الداخلة، وقياس قولهما في العتق أن يقولا هاهنا بسقوط ربع مهر الداخلة أيضاً. وأما على قول محمد له فلا حاجة إلى بيان الفرق ؛ فإنّه حكم في الصورتين على نمط واحد، حيث حكم في باب العتق بعتق ربع من دخل بالإيجاب الثاني، وحكم هاهنا بسقوط ثمن مهر من دخلت بالإيجاب الثاني.
[٤] قوله : إن الإيجاب الأول ... الخ ؛ خلاصته : الفرقُ أنَّ الثابت في مسألة العتق صالح لورود الإيجاب الثاني عليه، فيدخل في الإيجاب الثاني، ويوزع العتق الثابت به على الداخل والثابت فيعتق من الداخل النصف لعدم مانع يمنع عنه من الثابت ربعه لكون النصف الذي أصابه بالثاني شائعاً في نصفيه، وقد عتق نصفه بالإيجاب الأول، فيعتق بهذا الإيجاب الربع ، بخلافِ الثابتة في مسألة الطلاق، فإنّها مترددة بين كونها صالحة للإيجاب الثاني، وبين عدم صلوحها له.

Some scholars said: This is exclusively the statement of Muhammad. And it is said that it is also the statement of both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to this narration, both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) must differentiate between manumission and divorce: that the first pronouncement in manumission and divorce necessitated apportionment between the external and the fixed. When he died before clarification, it became clear that in the case of manumission, as he spoke, it became halved between them. There remained no subject for the second pronouncement; therefore, what the second affected entered into it and was shared among its portions, and what the first affected fell away as per the detailed explanation earlier. So too here. [1] His statement: 'this' refers to what was mentioned in the text: the fall of one-quarter of the dower of the one who entered (the marriage), one-eighth of the dower of the one who exited, and three-eighths of the fixed (wife). [2] His statement: 'exclusively' – as for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), one-quarter of the dower of the one who entered falls, as in the case of manumission. The justification of their statement and his statement in manumission has passed. [3] His statement: 'both must differentiate' – meaning that since the matter of divorce is agreed upon, they must explain the difference between the case of manumission and the case of divorce, where he said in the case of manumission: half of the external and internal (slaves) are freed, and in the case of divorce, one-quarter of the dower of the exiting wife and one-eighth of the dower of the entering wife fall. And by analogy with their statement in manumission, they would say here that one-quarter of the dower of the entering wife also falls. As for according to the statement of Muhammad, there is no need to explain the difference, for he ruled in both cases in a uniform manner: he ruled in the chapter of manumission that one-quarter of the one who entered by the second pronouncement is freed, and he ruled here that one-eighth of the dower of the one who entered by the second pronouncement falls. [4] His statement: 'the first pronouncement...etc.' – its summary: the difference is that the fixed (wife) in the case of manumission is suitable for the second pronouncement to occur upon her, so she enters into the second pronouncement, and the manumission established by it is distributed between the internal and the fixed. So half of the internal is freed because there is no preventing impediment, and from the fixed one-quarter is freed because the half that the second affected is shared between its halves, and half of it was already freed by the first pronouncement, so by this pronouncement one-quarter is freed. Unlike the fixed wife in the case of divorce, for she is ambiguous between being suitable for the second pronouncement and not being suitable for it. [0] His statement: 'necessitated' – for his statement addressing his two slaves: 'one of you is free' and likewise his statement to his two wives: 'one of you is divorced' necessitates apportionment between them, for if the intended from the ambiguous is that, even if he did not clarify. Because the principle in performative utterances is that their legal effect is established concurrently with speaking them unless a preventing impediment exists. In manumission, the intention for the external is opposed by the intention for the fixed, so the first pronouncement is distributed between them, until each becomes partially freed – this according to Abu Hanifa. Or he becomes ambiguous between freedom and slavery like a mukatab – this according to Abu Yusuf. [0] So the second pronouncement cannot be intended as a report due to falsehood, so it is a performative utterance, and there must be a subject. Thus the internal is entirely a subject, so half of him is freed. The fixed, if it were entirely a subject, would have half freed by this pronouncement. Since half of it is a subject, one-quarter of it is freed. And no other matter existed that would specify one of them for manumission or divorce from the matters that will be mentioned later. And if the master or husband died, judgment is given in the chapter of manumission that the first pronouncement necessitates freeing half of each of them, but not so in divorce. 11 His statement: 'unless a preventing impediment prevents' – like ambiguity and generality. So here, since his pronouncement was in the manner of ambiguity, it became dependent on his clarification, and no immediate ruling was given. After his death without clarification and without specifying his intent, it is judged that it necessitated apportionment from the beginning. [2] His statement: 'is opposed by' – because the one manumitted by the pronouncement is only one of them, and both are equal; there is no preference for the intention of the fixed over the intention of the external, nor for the intention of the external over the intention of the fixed. [3] His statement: 'is distributed' – passive imperfect from distribution, meaning division. Pause. [4] His statement: 'And this' – meaning his being partially freed according to him; because manumission is divisible in his view without hesitation and without [0] His statement: 'And this according to Abu Yusuf' – for each of them is ambiguous between being free and being enslaved like a mukatab in his view. He did not mention Muhammad, although his statement is also like the statement of Abu Yusuf in this principle, because he is in the process of explaining the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. [6] His statement: 'the report' – meaning about the freedom of the fixed. [7] His statement: 'due to falsehood' – because the fixed is certainly not free; rather, he is either partially freed or ambiguous like a mukatab.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. It deals with the ruling when a master says to two slaves 'one of you is free' (or a husband says to two wives 'one of you is divorced') and dies before specifying which one. The dispute centers on the effect of the first and any second pronouncement. The text presents the view that Muhammad's position is exclusive (or shared by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad holds a uniform ruling in both manumission and divorce: one-quarter of the one who entered by the second pronouncement is freed (or one-eighth of dower falls). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (on one narration) must differentiate: in manumission, the fixed slave is partially free and thus can be a subject for the second pronouncement; in divorce, the fixed wife is ambiguous, so the second pronouncement cannot fully affect her. The explanation shows the reasoning: the first pronouncement causes apportionment (tansif) between external and fixed because the intention is ambiguous. Upon death without clarification, it is judged that the first pronouncement operated from the start to free half of each slave (Abu Hanifa's view) or to create a state of ambiguity like a mukatab (Abu Yusuf's view). The second pronouncement cannot be a report (because false), so it is a performative requiring a subject. The internal is fully a subject; the fixed is only partially a subject (half freed), so the second pronouncement frees an additional quarter from the fixed. In divorce, the fixed wife is not fully subject to the second pronouncement (due to her ambiguous status), so the shares differ. The commentary enumerates the precise shares: one-quarter of dower of the entering wife falls, one-eighth of the exiting wife, three-eighths of the fixed wife – this is the ruling in the text.

Key Terms
الإيجاب (al-ījāb): The pronouncement or utterance that creates a legal effect, such as 'one of you is free' or 'one of you is divorced'.
الإبهام (al-ibhām): Ambiguity or lack of specification in a pronouncement, e.g., saying 'one of you' without naming which.
التنصيف (al-tanṣīf): Apportionment into halves; the legal effect that distributes the pronouncement equally between the two parties.
الداخلة (al-dākhilah): The wife who entered the marriage (or the slave who was acquired later); the one who becomes the subject of the second pronouncement.
الخارجة (al-khārijah): The wife who exited the marriage (i.e., the one who was already married at the time of the first pronouncement); or the existing slave.
الثابتة (al-thābitah): The fixed wife (or slave) — the one who was the subject of the first pronouncement and remains ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the practical consequence of Abu Yusuf's view that the first pronouncement creates ambiguity (taraddud) like a mukatab?
A) The fixed slave is immediately free half
B) The fixed slave's status is ambiguous and cannot be a full subject for the second pronouncement
C) The second pronouncement is invalid
D) Only the internal slave is affected by the second pronouncement

Key Takeaway
The effect of a second ambiguous pronouncement in manumission and divorce differs among Hanafi imams due to the subjecthood of the fixed party.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Ambiguous Manumission: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Contrast with Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ambiguous manumission with contrast to divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's and Abu Yusuf's positions on ambiguous manumission, explain the reasoning behind each, and distinguish why the same splitting does not apply to ambiguous divorce.

Core Idea
In ambiguous manumission, the first utterance is split (tawzi'), but in divorce splitting is impossible because partial divorce implies full divorce.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal effect of an ambiguous manumission utterance when the master dies without specifying his intent. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the first utterance is distributed equally, resulting in each slave being partially free, while Imam Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad) view the slaves as in a state of fluctuation, similar to a mukatib. The passage then contrasts this with ambiguous divorce, highlighting a key difference: a wife cannot be partially divorced. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principles of insha' and divisibility in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle for enactive statements
Start by noting the foundational rule: rulings accompany enactive utterances (insha'at) unless a preventing factor exists. Here, ambiguity (ibham) is that preventing factor.
This principle is the basis for both manumission and divorce analysis.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its rationale
Abu Hanifa holds that the first utterance is distributed (yuwazza') between the two slaves, making each partially free. His reasoning: both slaves are equal in the master's intent, and manumission is divisible. The utterance's effect is apportioned.
Key term: tawzi' (distribution). Manumission's divisibility is crucial.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and its rationale
Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad) hold that each slave becomes in a state of fluctuation (taraddud) between freedom and slavery, like a mukatib. Their reasoning: the ambiguous utterance cannot fully affect either slave; it leaves them in suspense until clarification. They analogize to the mukatib's intermediate status.
Key term: taraddud (fluctuation). The mukatib analogy provides a middle status.
4
Contrast with ambiguous divorce
The passage explains why the same splitting does not apply to divorce: a wife cannot be partially divorced. A ruling of 'half divorced' would make her fully divorced. Therefore, the first utterance in divorce is not split; only one wife is divorced entirely. The second utterance's effect is calculated based on dower shares.
Divorce's indivisibility prevents tawzi'. This shows the importance of the nature of the legal act.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa, each slave is partially free and can earn the remainder. According to Abu Yusuf, each slave is like a mukatib, retaining obligations and rights of a slave until full freedom is achieved. In divorce, the result is that one wife is fully divorced, and dower adjustments apply.
The practical difference affects the slaves' status and the couple's financial rights.

لأن الأصل في الإنشاءات أن يثبت حكمها مقارناً للتكلم بهما إلا أن يمنع مانع ، ففي العتق إرادة الخارج تعارضها إرادة الثابت ، فالإيجاب الأول يوزع بينهما ، حتى صار كل واحد معتق البعض ، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة له ، أو يصير متردداً بين الحرية والرقية كالمكاتب ، وهذا عند أبي يوسف (0)

ولم يوجد أمر آخر يعيّن أحدهما للعتق أو الطلاق من الأمور التي سيأتي ذكرها ، ومات المولى أو الزوج يحكم في باب العتق بكون الإيجاب الأول موجباً لعتق نصف كلّ واحد منهما، ولا كذلك في الطلاق.
قوله : إلا أن يمنع مانع ؛ كالإبهام والإجمال، فهاهنا لما كان إيجابه على طريقة الإبهام صار متوقفاً على بيانه، ولم يحكم بأمرٍ على فور تكمله، وبعد موته من غير بيان، وعدم تعيين مراده يحكم بأنه كان موجباً للتنصيف من الابتداء. قوله : تعارضها ؛ لأنّ المعتق بإيجاب إنّما هو أحدهما، وكلاهما مساويان، لا ترجيح لإرادة الثابت على إرادة الخارج، ولا لإرادة الخارج على إرادة الثابت. قوله : يوزع ؛ مضارع مجهول من التوزيع أي التقسيم.

وأما في الطلاق فلا يمكن أن يكون كلُّ واحدٍ منهما مطلقة البعض ؛ لأنَّ مطلقة البعض مطلقة كلها ، فلم يتنصف الإيجاب الأول، فالمطلقة إما الخارجة وإما الثابتة ، فإن كانت الثابتة طَلقَت بالأوّل، فلا حُكْمَ للإيجاب الثاني
قوله : وأما في الطلاق...الخ ؛ حاصله أنَّ الإيجاب الأول ؛ أي قوله لزوجيه : إحداكما طالق، وإن كان بظاهر يوجب التصنيف عند عدم ظهور المراد من المبهم، لكنّه غير ممكن هاهنا ؛ فإنّ الطلاق وكونها مطلقة لا يتجزأ، فمطلقة البعض مطلق كلّها على ما مر تفصيله في موضعه. فلو حكم بالإيجاب الأوّل أن نصف كلّ منهما مطلق ، لزم أن تكون كلّ واحدٍ منهما مطلّقة، وهو خلافُ إيجابه، فإنّ مقتضاه كون إحداهما مطلقة، لا كون كليهما مطلقتين.
فمن ثمّ حكم بأنه لا يتنصف الإيجاب الأوّل ، بل تكون ال ن المطلقة إحداهما فقط ، وهي إما الثابتة وإما الخارجة، فإن كانت المطلقة. هي الثابتة فقوله مرة أخرى للثابتة والداخلة : إحداكما طالق لا يوجب شيئاً لاحتمال أن يكون خبراً عن كون الثابتة مطلقة، بأن يكون المراد من إحداكما هو الثابتة ، وإذا كان إخباراً عن طلاق سابق لا يثبتُ بهذا الكلام شيء من الطلاق؛ لأنّ ثبوته ووقوعه إنّما هو عند كون الكلام الدال عليه إنشاء مسوقا لغرض إيقاعه، فعلى هذا التقدير لا يصح هذا الكلام على سبيل الإنشائية، ولا يكون إيجاباً.
وإن كانت المطلقة بالإيجاب الأوّل هي الخارجة، يمكن تصحيح الإيجاب الثاني على سبيل الإنشائية والإيقاعية ؛ لكونه دائرا بين الثابتة والداخلة ؛ لعدم كونهما مطلّقتين ، فلو كان الإيجاب الثاني صحيحاً من كل وجه، كما في صورة العتق ، أثبت حكم النصف بين الثابتة والداخلة، وتوزع عليهما بالسوية.
ولما لم يكن كذلك بل كان الإيجاب الثاني صحيحاً على سبيل الإنشائية من وجه دون وجه لم يثبت حكم النصف في الثابتة والداخلة، بل حكم نصفه وهو الربع ، ثمَّ انقسم ذلك الربع عليهما على السويّة فأصاب كل منهما مقدار الثمن، فسقط الداخلة الثمن لا الربع وسقط من مهر الثابتة ثمن بهذا الإيجاب، وثمنان بالإيجاب الأول ؛ أي الربع ، كما سقط الثمنان من الخارجة.
Book of Manumission: Ambiguous Manumission. Because the principle in enactments is that their ruling is established concurrently with the utterance unless prevented. In manumission, the intention to free the absent [slave] is opposed by the intention to free the present [slave], so the first utterance is distributed between them, so that each becomes a freed of a part. This according to Abu Hanifa. Or it becomes fluctuating between freedom and slavery like a mukatib, and this according to Abu Yusuf. The second utterance cannot be intended as a report because of falsehood, so it is an enactment; a locus is necessary. The entering [slave] entirely is a locus, so half of him is freed; the present [slave] if entirely a locus would be freed half by this utterance, so if half is a locus, a quarter is freed. There was no other matter determining one of them for manumission or divorce from matters that will be mentioned, and the master or husband died. In the chapter of manumission, it is ruled that the first utterance necessitates freeing half of each one of them, and not so in divorce. He said: 'Unless prevented'; like ambiguity and generalization. Here, because his utterance was in the manner of ambiguity, it became dependent on clarification, and no ruling is issued immediately like its completion, and after his death without clarification and without specifying his intent, it is ruled that it necessitated division into halves from the beginning. He said: 'It is opposed': because the freed by the utterance is only one of them, and both are equal, no preference for the intent of the present over the intent of the absent, nor for the intent of the absent over the intent of the present. He said: 'is distributed': passive present from 'distribution' meaning division. He said: 'and this': i.e., he is freed of a part according to him because manumission is divisible according to him without fluctuation or stoppage. He said: 'and this according to Abu Yusuf': for each one of them fluctuates between being free and being enslaved like a mukatib according to him, and he did not mention Muhammad, although his statement is also like the statement of Abu Yusuf in this principle, because he is in the context of explaining the school of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. He said: 'the report': i.e., about the freedom of the present. He said: 'because of falsehood': because the present is not definitely free, but rather he is either freed of a part or fluctuating like a mukatib. As for divorce, it cannot be that each of them is partially divorced, because a partially divorced woman is entirely divorced. So the first utterance is not halved. The divorced woman is either the absent or the present. If the present was divorced by the first, then there is no effect of the second utterance. He said: 'As for divorce...' etc.; its summary: the first utterance, i.e., his statement to his two wives 'One of you is divorced', even if in appearance it necessitates division when the intent of the ambiguous is not clear, but it is not possible here because divorce and being divorced are not divisible. A partially divorced woman is entirely divorced as the details came in its place. If it were ruled by the first utterance that half of each is divorced, it would necessitate that each of them is divorced, contrary to his utterance, for its requirement is that one of them is divorced, not both. Hence it is ruled that the first utterance is not halved, but rather the divorced woman is only one of them, either the present or the absent. If the divorced woman is the present, then his statement again to the present and the entering wife 'One of you is divorced' does not necessitate anything because of the possibility that it is a report about the present being divorced, in that the intended from 'one of you' is the present. If it is a report about a previous divorce, nothing of divorce is established by this speech, because its establishment and occurrence is only when the speech indicating it is an enactment aimed at effectuating it. On this assumption, this speech is not valid as enactive, and it is not an utterance. If the divorced by the first utterance is the absent, the second utterance can be valid as enactive and effectuating, because it revolves between the present and the entering wife, since they are not divorced. If the second utterance were valid in every respect, as in the form of manumission, it would establish the ruling of half between the present and the entering wife, and it would be equally distributed between them. But since it is not so, rather the second utterance is valid as enactive in some respects and not others, the ruling of half is not established for the present and the entering wife, but rather the ruling of half of it, which is a quarter. Then that quarter is divided between them equally, so each gets an eighth. So from the entering wife's dower falls an eighth, not a quarter, and from the present wife's dower falls an eighth by this utterance, and two-eighths by the first utterance, i.e., a quarter, just as two-eighths fell from the absent wife's dower.
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on al-Wiqayah, explaining the ruling of ambiguous manumission (al-'itq al-mubham) and its difference from ambiguous divorce (al-talaq al-mubham). The author begins by stating the general principle for enactive statements (insha'at): the ruling accompanies the utterance unless prevented. In the case of a master saying to two slaves 'One of you is free' and then dying before specifying, the first utterance is distributed between the two slaves because the master's intention to free one is opposed by the intention to free the other, and both are equal. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this results in each slave becoming partially free ('atiq al-ba'd), because manumission is divisible. According to Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad by agreement), each slave becomes in a state of fluctuation (taraddud) between freedom and slavery, like a mukatib. If the master then made a second similar utterance to a different set of slaves or to the same ones, the details become more complex. The passage then contrasts with divorce: if a husband says to his two wives 'One of you is divorced' and dies without specifying, the first utterance cannot be split because a wife cannot be partially divorced—partial divorce implies full divorce. Thus one of the wives is fully divorced, either the one present or the absent. If the present wife was divorced by the first utterance, a second analogous utterance has no effect because it could be interpreted as a report. If the absent wife was divorced, the second utterance can be a valid enactive statement, but its effect is limited to a quarter of the dower (mahr) distributed between the present and the entering wife, due to the impossibility of full splitting. This discussion shows the careful Hanafi reasoning in applying principles of insha' and qiyas to different types of legal acts.

Key Terms
العتق المبهم (al-'itq al-mubham): Ambiguous manumission, where the master says 'one of you is free' without specifying which slave, and then dies before clarifying.
الإيجاب الأول (al-ijab al-awwal): The first utterance of ambiguous manumission or divorce that is not clarified before death.
التوزيع (al-tawzi'): Distribution or splitting; here it refers to dividing the legal effect of the utterance equally between the two slaves.
المكاتب (al-mukatib): A slave who has made a contract with his master to purchase his freedom, and is in a state between freedom and slavery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the first ambiguous utterance in divorce not split as in manumission?
A) Because divorce is less common than manumission
B) Because a wife cannot be partially divorced; partial divorce implies full divorce
C) Because the husband's intention is more important in divorce
D) Because the wife is not a slave

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous manumission, the first utterance is split (tawzi') or causes fluctuation (taraddud), but in divorce splitting is impossible due to the indivisibility of divorce; this highlights how the nature of the legal act shapes its rulings.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
12 min
Indivisibility of Divorce in Ambiguous Pronouncements
Hanafi talil on why divorce cannot be divided

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that divorce is indivisible and calculate the mahr reduction when a second ambiguous pronouncement is made under uncertainty.

Core Idea
Divorce does not divide: a woman declared partially divorced is fully divorced.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling: when a man makes two successive ambiguous divorce pronouncements involving multiple wives, divorce cannot be fractionally applied. Unlike manumission, where partial freedom is possible, divorce is an all-or-nothing state. The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya unpacks the logical consequences, showing how the second pronouncement's legal effect is halved due to uncertainty, leading to a fractional reduction of mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the initial pronouncement
The man has two wives (kharija and thabita) and says 'One of you is divorced.' Recognise that the pronouncement is ambiguous—it must apply fully to one wife because divorce is indivisible.
Contrast with manumission, where partial freedom is possible.
2
Determine the two possible outcomes of the first pronouncement
Either the thabita or the kharija is divorced. If it is the thabita, the second pronouncement (to thabita and dakhila) is merely informative and creates no new divorce. If it is the kharija, the second pronouncement is valid but its effect is reduced.
3
Apply the indivisibility principle to the second pronouncement
If the kharija was divorced by the first pronouncement, the second pronouncement (to thabita and dakhila) is ambiguous again. It is valid on one interpretation (if the first pronouncement meant the kharija) and invalid on the other (if it meant the thabita). Because uncertainty halts full effect, the second pronouncement is considered 'half-valid'.
4
Calculate the mahr reduction
A fully valid second pronouncement would reduce mahr by half for each of thabita and dakhila (total quarter each). But due to half-validity, only half of that effect applies: each loses an eighth of her mahr from the second pronouncement. The kharija lost a quarter from the first pronouncement; thabita loses an additional eighth from the second.
Per source: 'half of half is a quarter' then divided equally.
5
Articulate the rule and its rationale
Divorce is indivisible because it is a complete dissolution of marriage—partial divorce is a contradiction. Therefore, ambiguous pronouncements must be resolved by giving full effect to one wife, and subsequent ambiguous pronouncements are partially valid when they could be mere information.
The ratio legis (illah) is the indivisible nature of divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في الطلاق فلا يمكن أن يكون كلُّ واحدٍ منهما مطلقة البعض ؛ لأنَّ مطلقة البعض مطلقة كلها ، فلم يتنصف الإيجاب الأول، فالمطلقة إما الخارجة وإما الثابتة ، فإن كانت الثابتة طَلقَت بالأوّل، فلا حُكْمَ للإيجاب الثاني

قوله : وأما في الطلاق...الخ ؛ حاصله أنَّ الإيجاب الأول ؛ أي قوله لزوجيه : إحداكما طالق، وإن كان بظاهر يوجب التصنيف عند عدم ظهور المراد من المبهم، لكنّه غير ممكن هاهنا ؛ فإنّ الطلاق وكونها مطلقة لا يتجزأ، فمطلقة البعض مطلق كلّها على ما مر تفصيله في موضعه. فلو حكم بالإيجاب الأوّل أن نصف كلّ منهما مطلق ، لزم أن تكون كلّ واحدٍ منهما مطلّقة، وهو خلافُ إيجابه، فإنّ مقتضاه كون إحداهما مطلقة، لا كون كليهما مطلقتين.

فمن ثمّ حكم بأنه لا يتنصف الإيجاب الأوّل ، بل تكون المطلقة إحداهما فقط ، وهي إما الثابتة وإما الخارجة، فإن كانت المطلقة هي الثابتة فقوله مرة أخرى للثابتة والداخلة : إحداكما طالق لا يوجب شيئاً لاحتمال أن يكون خبراً عن كون الثابتة مطلقة، بأن يكون المراد من إحداكما هو الثابتة ، وإذا كان إخباراً عن طلاق سابق لا يثبتُ بهذا الكلام شيء من الطلاق؛ لأنّ ثبوته ووقوعه إنّما هو عند كون الكلام الدال عليه إنشاء مسوقا لغرض إيقاعه، فعلى هذا التقدير لا يصح هذا الكلام على سبيل الإنشائية، ولا يكون إيجاباً.

وإن كانت المطلقة بالإيجاب الأوّل هي الخارجة، يمكن تصحيح الإيجاب الثاني على سبيل الإنشائية والإيقاعية ؛ لكونه دائرا بين الثابتة والداخلة ؛ لعدم كونهما مطلّقتين ، فلو كان الإيجاب الثاني صحيحاً من كل وجه، كما في صورة العتق ، أثبت حكم النصف بين الثابتة والداخلة، وتوزع عليهما بالسوية.

ولما لم يكن كذلك بل كان الإيجاب الثاني صحيحاً على سبيل الإنشائية من وجه دون وجه لم يثبت حكم النصف في الثابتة والداخلة، بل حكم نصفه وهو الربع ، ثمَّ انقسم ذلك الربع عليهما على السويّة فأصاب كل منهما مقدار الثمن، فسقط من مهر الداخلة الثمن لا الربع وسقط من مهر الثابتة ثمن بهذا الإيجاب، وثمنان بالإيجاب الأول ؛ أي الربع ، كما سقط من مهر الخارجة الثمنان.

لأنه يمكن أن يراد به الإخبار ، وإن كانت الخارجة ، فالإيجاب الثاني يكون دائرا بين الثابتة والداخلة على السويَّة ، فيثبت ربعه ؛ لأنَّ الإيجاب الثاني باطل على أحد التقديرين، وهو إرادة الثابتة بالإيجاب الأول، وهو صحيح على التقدير الآخر، وهو نصف التقديرين، فينتصف ، ونصفُ النّصفِ ربع ، فيسقط به ثمنُ المهر.
As for divorce, it is not possible for each of them to be partially divorced, because a woman partially divorced is fully divorced. Thus the first pronouncement is not divided; the divorced woman is either the exiting one or the remaining one. If the remaining one was divorced by the first, the second pronouncement has no effect.

[Commentator's words]: 'As for divorce...etc.'; his summary is that the first pronouncement, i.e., his saying to his two wives 'One of you is divorced', although in appearance necessitates division when the intended meaning from the ambiguous is not apparent, yet it is not possible here; because divorce and being divorced are not divisible. A woman partially divorced is fully divorced, as previously detailed in its place. If it were judged by the first pronouncement that half of each is divorced, then each one would be divorced, which contradicts his pronouncement, for its implication is that one of them is divorced, not both.

Therefore, it is judged that the first pronouncement is not divided; rather the divorced one is only one of them, either the remaining or the exiting. If the divorced one is the remaining, then his saying again to the remaining and the entering: 'One of you is divorced' does not effect anything, because it can be news about the remaining being divorced, such that the intended meaning of 'one of you' is the remaining. And if it is informing about a previous divorce, nothing of divorce is established by this speech; because its establishment and occurrence are only when the speech indicating it is a construction (insha) intended for effecting it. So on this assumption, this speech is not valid as construction, and it is not a pronouncement.

And if the divorced woman by the first pronouncement is the exiting one, it is possible to validate the second pronouncement as construction and effectual; because it circulates between the remaining and the entering; due to them not being divorced. If the second pronouncement were valid in every respect, as in the case of manumission, it would establish the ruling of half between the remaining and the entering, and it would be distributed equally between them.

But since it is not so, rather the second pronouncement is valid as construction in one respect but not another, it does not establish the ruling of half in the remaining and the entering; rather the ruling of its half, which is a quarter. Then that quarter is divided between them equally, so each gets an eighth. Thus from the mahr of the entering an eighth is removed, not a quarter; and from the mahr of the remaining an eighth is removed by this pronouncement, and two eighths by the first pronouncement – i.e., a quarter – and also from the mahr of the exiting two eighths are removed.

Because it can be intended as informing, and if the exiting (was meant), the second pronouncement circulates between the remaining and the entering equally, so its quarter is established; because the second pronouncement is invalid on one of the two possibilities (the intention of the remaining by the first pronouncement) and valid on the other possibility, which is half of the two possibilities. So it is halved, and half of half is a quarter, so by it an eighth of the mahr is removed.
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal analysis of an ambiguous divorce scenario where a man first says to his two wives (the 'remaining' and 'exiting') 'One of you is divorced', and later says to the remaining and another wife (the 'entering') 'One of you is divorced'. The commentator explains why the ruling differs from the analogous case of ambiguous manumission. The key point is that divorce, unlike manumission, cannot be divided: a woman declared partially divorced is fully divorced. Therefore, the first pronouncement must affect only one wife entirely. If it affected the remaining wife, the second pronouncement is merely informational and creates no new divorce. If it affected the exiting wife, the second pronouncement is a valid construction but its effect is halved because on one interpretation it is invalid (if the first intended the remaining) and on the other valid (if the first intended the exiting). Consequently, the mahr reduction is calculated as half of half, i.e., a quarter of the total mahr, distributed equally between the remaining and entering wives, so each loses an eighth.

Key Terms
مطلقة البعض (mutallaqat al-ba'd): A woman declared partially divorced – effectively fully divorced because divorce is indivisible.
ثابتة (thabita): The wife who remains (the one not leaving? The text uses 'thabita' for the wife who stays in the house, as opposed to 'kharija' who exits?). In this passage, it refers to the wife present at both times.
خارجة (kharija): The wife who exits (the one who was possibly divorced by the first pronouncement?).
داخلة (dakhila): The wife who enters (the new wife added after the first pronouncement).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi analysis, why does the second pronouncement ('One of you is divorced') result in only a quarter total mahr reduction rather than a half?
A) Because the husband intended only a quarter
B) Because uncertainty halves the effect: the pronouncement is valid on only one of two possible interpretations
C) Because the wives agreed to a reduced mahr
D) Because the first pronouncement already reduced the mahr by half

Key Takeaway
Divorce is indivisible; ambiguous pronouncements must fully affect one wife, and subsequent ambiguous pronouncements are partially valid due to uncertainty, with mahr reduction halved accordingly.
